Manager</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C1iOQHoV0Ik/YKL5qxeKbJI/AAAAAAAAQhs/1w4FKY01oGArJg_Qyl2JpI6YAOXc4v4PQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/AndroidWearOS-01.png\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> We‚Äôre announcing our biggest update yet to the Wear platform, with new features, APIs and tools to help developers create beautiful, high quality wearable experiences. In this blog post we highlight how we‚Äôre making it easier to build great apps for Wear, and how you can start working with pre-release versions of these APIs and tools to prepare your app for the new platform. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kYIb9g1r4lw\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2><strong>First things first: tools</strong></h2> <p> The first thing you‚Äôll want to do is download and install <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/preview\">Android Studio Arctic Fox Beta</a>, which includes a developer preview of the new Wear system image as well as improved tools for developing and testing Wear apps without a device: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Emulator with new Wear system image (preview) </strong>- A developer preview of the new Wear system image is now available so that you can use and play with the newest platform updates! <li><strong>Wear app to phone pairing</strong> - We‚Äôve made it much simpler to pair Wear emulators with your phone directly from Android Studio, so you can stay in the IDE to develop, test, and iterate. The new pairing assistant guides you step by step through pairing Wear emulators with physical or virtual phones directly in Android Studio! You can start by going to <em>Device Dropdown &gt; Wear OS emulator pairing assistant</em>. Note that this will currently pair with the Wear OS 2 companion, and a Wear companion for the new release will be coming soon. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/apps/creating#pairing-assistant\">Learn more</a>. <li><strong>Virtual Heart Rate Sensor</strong> - The emulator now has a virtual heart rate sensor, including support for the Heart Rate Sensor API, to help you create and test apps that respond differently to activity levels. <em>Make sure you are running at least Android Emulator v30.4.5 downloaded via the Android Studio SDK Manager.<br /></em> </li> </li></li> \n    </ul> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FjliXLO0Gw0/YKL2TF8TRqI/AAAAAAAAQhU/uTHckQkFgVIz_HIz-Ug5EWUwRbiYQZUFACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/heart_rate.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\" New Virtual Heart Rate Sensor in the Wear emulator allows the virtual heart rate to be adjusted with a slider bar \" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FjliXLO0Gw0/YKL2TF8TRqI/AAAAAAAAQhU/uTHckQkFgVIz_HIz-Ug5EWUwRbiYQZUFACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/heart_rate.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> We also announced a new watch face design tool built by Samsung. This new tool will make it a breeze to develop watch faces for all devices running Wear, and is coming soon. </p> <p> <strong>New developer documentation and design guidance</strong> </p> <p> In preparation for the new version of Wear we‚Äôve completely revamped our <a href=\"https://d.android.com/wear\">developer site</a> with new API documentation, learning pathways, codelabs and samples. And with Wear soon to feature a completely new consumer experience based on the latest from Material Design, we‚Äôve updated our design guidelines to cover the new design system, UI components, UX patterns, and styles. <a href=\"http://developer.android.com/training/wearables/design\">Learn more</a>. </p> <h2><strong>New Jetpack APIs</strong></h2> <p> From new Jetpack APIs tailored for small (round or square) screens and designed to optimize battery life to the Jetpack Tiles API, we‚Äôre adding a number of new features to help you build great Wear experiences, reduce boilerplate code, and write code that works consistently across Wear versions and devices: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Tiles</strong> - Tiles give users fast, predictable access to the information and actions they rely on most. We‚Äôve now opened up Tiles for developers, and we‚Äôve already been working with several early access partners to add Tiles to their apps. Here are a few coming soon: </li> \n    </ul> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-W_s73Ka5ykA/YKPsBNo3H4I/AAAAAAAAQj8/oVgkYGSmAOA6zaMJsZmPH73k8ItpOk5QwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-05-18%2Bat%2B12.31.16%2BPM.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"New tiles in development from Adidas, Sleep Cycle, Hole 19, Outdooractive, Calm, Flo, and Golfpad\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-W_s73Ka5ykA/YKPsBNo3H4I/AAAAAAAAQj8/oVgkYGSmAOA6zaMJsZmPH73k8ItpOk5QwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-05-18%2Bat%2B12.31.16%2BPM.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p>The Tiles API is in alpha and supported on devices running Wear OS 2 and up, so you can create Tiles for all the devices in the Wear ecosystem. Tiles will start to show up on consumer watches with the new platform update. <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/Btl5anJNvAs/ https://developer.android.com/training/articles/wear-tiles\"> </a> Learn more </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Task switching and Ongoing Activities</strong> - The new version of Wear makes it easy for users to switch back and forth between apps. With a minimal amount of code, you can use the new Ongoing Activities API to let your users return to your app after they‚Äôve navigated away (to start some other task such as music playback) by tapping an activity indicator icon at the bottom of the watch face, double tapping on the the side button, or via the <em>Recents</em> section of the global app launcher. The Ongoing Activities API is now in alpha. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/ongoing-activity\">Learn more</a>. </li> \n    </ul> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-pBRemH8oweM/YKL4PlefviI/AAAAAAAAQhk/woRHRsG5Abg44n9zNywQ4teYTiNYD3YygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/gif%2Bpage%2B%25281%2529.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100\" alt=\"3 new ways for users to switch between apps: Activity indicator on the watch face; double tap the watch‚Äôs side button; the Global app launcher\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-pBRemH8oweM/YKL4PlefviI/AAAAAAAAQhk/woRHRsG5Abg44n9zNywQ4teYTiNYD3YygCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/gif%2Bpage%2B%25281%2529.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> \n    <ul> \n     <li><strong>Health Services</strong> - We also announced today the beginning of a health and fitness platform, created in collaboration with Samsung. This platform provides fitness and health data generated from sensors, contextually-aware algorithms, and all-day health monitoring. You can use the APIs to create high quality, powerful fitness and health experiences for wearables with a simpler development experience. The platform handles all the work to manage your hardware and sensors for you, removing one of the biggest challenges in managing it yourself - knowing when to stop work so the battery doesn't drain. The alpha of this Health Services platform is available today. <a href=\"http://developer.android.com/training/wearables/health-services\">Learn more</a>. <li><strong>Other new APIs</strong> - We‚Äôve released several other new APIs in Jetpack to make wearable app development easier, including support for curved text, input, watch faces, complications and remote interactions. You can learn more about these APIs <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/wear#new-features\">here</a>. </li> </li> \n    </ul> <h2><strong>Google Play Store changes</strong></h2> <p> We know that user engagement and discovery of an app is an important part of growing your business, so big updates coming to Google Play will soon make it much easier for users to discover great app experiences on the watch, including using search to easily find apps for the watch, look at the Wear category for app recommendations, and install apps to the watch directly from the phone. </p> <h2> Learn more </h2> <p> We‚Äôre excited for the next generation of Wear. To learn more about developing apps for smartwatches, see <a href=\"http://d.android.com/wear\">d.android.com/wear</a>. href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-H4nSXL6IHdo/YKLF9UVsSnI/AAAAAAAAQgc/ctwAtZWsk7gZQAVJK22zmgDe4t1YHlVowCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/AndroidNewInTv_1024x512-V3.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android TV\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-H4nSXL6IHdo/YKLF9UVsSnI/AAAAAAAAQgc/ctwAtZWsk7gZQAVJK22zmgDe4t1YHlVowCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/AndroidNewInTv_1024x512-V3.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n  </center> <p> Today at Google I/O 2021, we announced a significant milestone for our team: we have over 80 million monthly active devices on Android TV OS, with more than 80% growth in the US alone. We would not be here without the hard work of the developer community, so a huge and heartfelt thank you to you all.</p> \n  <center> \n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/8rMPZlwvb5c\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n  </center> <p> Android TV OS is the operating system that powers a number of devices around the world including the new Google TV experience launched last fall. Google TV has generated a lot of excitement from consumers, developers, and industry partners alike, offering a content forward TV experience that helps the user discover more of the movies and shows they love. Google TV is available on streaming devices like the Chromecast with Google TV, smart TVs from Sony (and soon TCL!), and as an app on Android devices. Check out this <a href=\"https://youtu.be/O3BhUSEu8gg\">presentation</a> on how to get your app ready for Google TV. </p> <p> Our goal is to always enable you to build better and more engaging experiences on Android TV OS. One example of this is the widely utilized Watch Next API which increases app re-engagement by ~30% in certain cases<sup>1</sup>. Well over 100 major media partners are already using WatchNext API and you can learn more about how to add your app <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/tv/discovery/watch-next-add-programs\">here</a>. </p> <p> We are also announcing several new tools and helpful features to make developing for Android TV OS easier and enable you to create engaging experiences for your users. Some are already available and some will be available soon: </p> \n  <ul> \n   <li> <em>Cast Connect with Stream Transfer and Stream Expansion</em><a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/docs/android_tv_receiver/core_features\">: Cast Connect</a> allows users to cast from their phone/ tablet or Chrome browser onto your app on Android TV. Stream Transfer and Stream Expansion allow users to transfer media to other devices and/or play audio on multiple devices. </li> \n   <li> <em>Emulator updates:</em> To help you make your app work better on Google TV without requiring new hardware, we are now making our first Google TV Emulator available, running on Android 11. There will also be an Android 11 image with the traditional Android TV experience. You can now also use a remote that more closely mimics TV remotes directly within the Emulator. </li> \n   <li> <em>Firebase Test Lab:</em> Firebase Test Lab runs millions of tests every week on behalf of developers. Following requests from developers, we are excited to share that Firebase Test Lab is adding Android TV support. Firebase Test Lab Virtual Devices run your app in the cloud on Android TV emulators and allow you to scale your test across hundreds or thousands of virtual devices. Physical Devices will be coming soon. </li> \n   <li> <em>Android 12 Beta 1:</em> We are making the Android 12 Beta 1 available for TV on ADT-3 today. With this release the developer community will be able to take advantage of many of the changes and improvements coming with Android 12. We encourage you to try it and provide us with feedback. </li> \n  </ul> <p> Thank you for your continued support of the Android TV OS platform. The future of TV is bright and we can‚Äôt wait to see what you build next! </p> <p> <sup>1</sup> Average gain in number of days active in the app in a 28-day period amongst app 28DAUs, based on 3 apps analyzed during the 11/2020 - 2/2021 period. </p> \n  <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n   <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=iBszikqLEhI:JKasdkjD3x4:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img +0000","feedId":7,"bgimg":"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-H4nSXL6IHdo/YKLF9UVsSnI/AAAAAAAAQgc/ctwAtZWsk7gZQAVJK22zmgDe4t1YHlVowCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/AndroidNewInTv_1024x512-V3.png","linkMd5":"77d8e618556ef6c81843567cfa08d4a2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn18@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-14-924_f2d2e653ee6be5c3.webp","destWidth":2134,"destHeight":1067,"sourceBytes":27595,"destBytes":39876,"author":"Android 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"What‚Äôs new in Android 12 Beta","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/hGLAJopHf04/whats-new-in-android-12-beta.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tLt-TVPqpjA/YKMRwRPMfjI/AAAAAAAAQik/JNtMesFZ2i87RyBACHAVEC14CvcU7G__wCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-05-17%2Bat%2B9.00.30%2BPM.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Dave Burke, VP of Engineering </em><p> \n    <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\"> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2WiKDQwO6nI/YC2vlLLtUyI/AAAAAAAAQFM/lje72qqUt74m22FTZZx_0VmfFnfjODSiACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img id=\"floatRight\" alt=\"Android 12 logo\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2WiKDQwO6nI/YC2vlLLtUyI/AAAAAAAAQFM/lje72qqUt74m22FTZZx_0VmfFnfjODSiACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" /></a> \n    </div> <p> Today at <a href=\"https://events.google.com/io/\">Google I/O</a> we unveiled the first Beta of Android 12, one of our most ambitious releases ever. We focused on a new UI that adapts to you, improving performance, with privacy and security at the core. For developers, we‚Äôre giving you more tools to build delightful experiences for people on phones, laptops, tablets, wearables, TVs, and cars. </p> <p> There‚Äôs a lot to explore in Beta 1, starting with the most significant UI update to Android yet, created with a design language that we call <a href=\"https://material.io/blog/announcing-material-you\">Material You</a>. There are new privacy features to try too, like approximate location, and a new standard called Performance Class that lets apps and users identify high-performing devices. </p> <p> Try Android 12 Beta today on Pixel devices by <a href=\"https://www.google.com/android/beta\">enrolling here</a>. Thanks to our device-maker partners who are working to accelerate updates, you can now get the Beta on other devices as well, including select devices from ASUS, OnePlus, Oppo, Realme, Sharp, TCL, Transsion, Vivo, Xiaomi, and ZTE, with others on the way. Visit <a href=\"https://android.com/beta\">android.com/beta</a> to learn more. </p> <p> Read on for more highlights of what‚Äôs new and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12\">visit the Android 12 developer site</a> for details on everything in Android 12 and how to get started developing. </p> <h2><strong>A new UI for Android</strong></h2> <p> As we highlighted in our <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android/android-12-beta\">consumer blog post</a>, Android 12 brings the biggest design change in Android's history. We rethought the entire experience, from the colors to the shapes, light and motion, making Android 12 more expressive, dynamic, and personal. This work is being done in deep collaboration between our software, hardware and Material Design teams, and we‚Äôre unifying our software and hardware ecosystems under a single design language called <a href=\"https://material.io/blog/announcing-material-you\">Material You</a>. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/hGLAJopHf04/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SbNslCeckd8/YKMMSibcdXI/AAAAAAAAQh0/AHE9ssE2i0sx_CZOJY5Nf-07tYH4kxA2wCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.jpeg \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android 12 UI\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SbNslCeckd8/YKMMSibcdXI/AAAAAAAAQh0/AHE9ssE2i0sx_CZOJY5Nf-07tYH4kxA2wCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.jpeg \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> We‚Äôve extended the new design language across the platform and UI components, so your apps will get these upgrades automatically. </p> <p> <strong>Redesigned widgets</strong> - Along with the design changes in Android 12 we‚Äôve refreshed app widgets to make them more useful, beautiful, and discoverable. We added <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets#new-compound-buttons\">new interactive controls</a> like checkboxes, switches, and radio buttons and made <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets#apply-configuration-options\">personalizing widgets easier</a>. Android 12 widgets look great with our system UI and themes, with rounded corners and padding automatically adapted to every launcher and home screen. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets#provide-responsive-layouts\">Responsive layouts</a> let you adapt widgets to phones, tablets, foldables, and other screens. We also added <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/hGLAJopHf04/ https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets#dynamic-colors\">dynamic color APIs</a> so your widgets can use system colors to create a personalized but consistent look. And we‚Äôre making widgets easier to discover through an improved widget picker and an integration with the Assistant. Check out <a href=\"https://github.com/android/user-interface-samples/tree/main/AppWidget\">sample code</a> and give the updated widgets a try. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets\">More here</a>. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/hGLAJopHf04/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-nMtiWDRBRB8/YKMMpO0Vz2I/AAAAAAAAQh8/ZbNKF2l9_TUCLgfnyBxF-3yEzwKOJmlYwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/blue%2Bwidgets.png \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:360px\" alt=\"widgets in Android 12\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-nMtiWDRBRB8/YKMMpO0Vz2I/AAAAAAAAQh8/ZbNKF2l9_TUCLgfnyBxF-3yEzwKOJmlYwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/blue%2Bwidgets.png \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <br> <p> <strong>Stretch overscroll</strong> - We‚Äôre also adding a new system-wide ‚Äústretch‚Äù overscroll effect to let users know they‚Äôve scrolled past the end of the available content in your UI. The stretch effect provides a natural vertical and horizontal scroll-stop indicator that‚Äôs common across all apps, and it‚Äôs enabled by default for scrolling containers across the platform and AndroidX. The new stretch overscroll replaces the glow overscroll supported in previous versions. Make sure to test your apps and content with the new scrolling behavior, and if needed you can opt out. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/overscroll\">More here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Smoother audio transitions </strong>- UI isn't just about the visuals. We've also improved the way that audio focus is handled. When an app loses audio focus, its audio is automatically faded out, providing a smoother transition between apps which play audio, and preventing apps from playing over each other. This is particularly relevant in foldable and multi-screen Android environments. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/audio-focus-improvements\">More here.</a> </p> <h2><strong>Performance</strong></h2> <p> With Android 12, we‚Äôve made significant and deep investments in performance - from foundational performance that makes the system and apps faster and smoother, to a new standard for high-performing devices that helps developers deliver richer experiences on those devices. </p> <p> <strong>Faster, more efficient system performance</strong> - We reduced the CPU time needed for core system services by 22%, so devices will be faster and more responsive. We also improved Android's power efficiency by reducing the use of big cores by the system server by 15% to help devices run longer before needing to charge. </p> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3InI7FNnLWE/YKMNQZlgzVI/AAAAAAAAQiE/wLmymP8zKvYJsXWV5D-0PGa8qDpXtrhaQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screenshot%2Bfrom%2B2021-05-13%2B15-09-28.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Sampled rate , omn big core\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3InI7FNnLWE/YKMNQZlgzVI/AAAAAAAAQiE/wLmymP8zKvYJsXWV5D-0PGa8qDpXtrhaQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screenshot%2Bfrom%2B2021-05-13%2B15-09-28.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     </center> <p> We improved transitions and app startup times by reducing lock contention and latency variability, and we optimized I/O for faster app loading. In PackageManager, a read-only snapshot reduced lock contention by as much as 92%. In Binder, lightweight caching radically improved latencies up to 47x in targeted calls. In I/O, we accelerated dex/odex/vdex files to improve app load times, especially on low-memory phones. Our restriction on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#notification-trampolines\">notification trampolines</a> also helps reduce latency for apps started from a notification. For example, the Google Photos app now launches 34% faster after moving away from notification trampolines. </p> <p> To improve database query performance we‚Äôve optimized CursorWindow by inlining results in Binder transactions. For small windows, CursorWindow is 36% faster, and for windows over 1000 rows the improvements are as high as 49x. </p> <p> <strong>Performance class</strong> - Starting with Android 12 and working together with our ecosystem partners, we‚Äôre introducing a common standard for high-performing Android devices. </p> <p> This standard, called <em>performance class</em>, defines a set of capabilities that go beyond Android's baseline requirements. Devices that meet the performance class requirements can support more demanding use-cases and deliver higher quality content. Developers can <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION.html#MEDIA_PERFORMANCE_CLASS\">check for performance class at runtime</a> and then reliably deliver enhanced experiences that take full advantage of the device‚Äôs performance. </p> <p> Initially, we‚Äôre focusing performance class capabilities on media use-cases, with requirements including camera startup latency, codec availability and encoding quality, as well as minimum memory size, screen resolution and read/write performance. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/performance-class\">More here.</a> </p> <h2><strong>Private by design</strong></h2> <p> Privacy is at the heart of everything we do, and in Android 12 we‚Äôre continuing to give people more transparency and control while keeping their devices and data secure. Today we announced several new privacy features that will be coming in Beta 2 - Privacy Dashboard, microphone and camera indicators, and microphone and camera toggles. Stay tuned for more on these features. Here‚Äôs what‚Äôs new in Beta 1. </p> <p> <strong>App hibernation</strong> - Last year we launched <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/11/privacy/permissions#auto-reset\">permissions auto-reset</a>, and over the last two weeks, Android has reset permissions for over 8.5 million apps that weren‚Äôt being used - so apps that people have forgotten about can‚Äôt still access their data. In Android 12 we‚Äôre building on permissions auto-reset by intelligently hibernating apps that have gone unused for an extended period - optimizing for device storage, performance and safety. Hibernation not only revokes permissions granted previously by the user, but it also force-stops the app and reclaims memory, storage and other temporary resources. In this state the system also prevents apps from running jobs in the background or receiving push notifications, helping to keep users safe. Hibernation should be transparent for most apps, but if needed, direct users to Settings to turn off this feature for your app. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#app-hibernation\">More here</a>. </p> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\"> \n      <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-t2u1XR8xvbI/YKMN1bW8sQI/AAAAAAAAQiM/DkHHleEwSjguvbYnZQ5camGJYLnnxq1MQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Location_Accuracy_Android12.gif\" style=\"display: block; padding: -10em; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:260px\" id=\"floatRight\" alt=\"Android 12 device location\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"784\" data-original-width=\"784\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-t2u1XR8xvbI/YKMN1bW8sQI/AAAAAAAAQiM/DkHHleEwSjguvbYnZQ5camGJYLnnxq1MQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Location_Accuracy_Android12.gif \" /></a> \n     </div> <p> <strong>Nearby device permissions</strong> - Previously, Bluetooth scanning required apps to have the location permission, which was a challenge for apps that needed to pair with nearby devices but didn‚Äôt actually need the device location. We‚Äôre now allowing apps to scan for nearby devices without needing location permission. Apps targeting Android 12 can scan using the new <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission.html#BLUETOOTH_SCAN\">BLUETOOTH_SCAN</a></code> permission with the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/R.attr.html#usesPermissionFlags\">usesPermissionFlags=\"neverForLocation\"</a> </code>attribute. After pairing with a device, use the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission.html#BLUETOOTH_CONNECT\">BLUETOOTH_CONNECT</a></code> permission to interact with it. These permissions promote privacy-friendly app design while reducing friction for apps. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/bluetooth-permissions\">More here</a>. <p> <strong>Approximate location</strong> - Recently we‚Äôve given people better ways to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/location/permissions\">manage access to location</a>, such as through separate permissions for foreground and background access and an ‚Äúonly this time‚Äù option. Now for apps targeting Android 12, we‚Äôre offering even more control with a new ‚Äúapproximate location‚Äù option. When apps request precise location data, users can now choose to grant either precise or approximate location. Users can also change an app‚Äôs location precision at any time from Settings. If your app requests precise location data (<code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission#ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION\">ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION</a></code>), keep these changes in mind and make sure your app functions properly with approximate location only. For almost all general uses of location, we recommend asking for approximate location (<code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission#ACCESS_COARSE_LOCATION\">ACCESS_COARSE_LOCATION</a></code>) only. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#approximate-location\">More here</a>. <h2><strong>App compatibility</strong></h2> <p> If you haven‚Äôt tested your app for compatibility with Android 12 yet, now is the time to do it! With Android 12 in Beta, we‚Äôre opening up access to early-adopter users as well as developers, on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/devices\">Pixel and other devices</a>. This means that in the weeks ahead, expect many more users to be trying your app on Android 12 and raising any issues that they find. </p> <p> To test for compatibility, install your published app from Google Play or other source on a device or emulator running Android 12 Beta and work through all of the app‚Äôs flows. Review the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-all\">behavior changes</a> to focus your testing. After you‚Äôve resolved any issues, publish an update as soon as possible. </p> <p> With Beta we‚Äôre getting closer to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/overview#platform_stability\">Platform Stability</a> in August 2021. Starting then, app-facing system behaviors, SDK/NDK APIs, and non-SDK lists will be finalized. At that time, finish up your final compatibility testing and release a fully compatible version of your app, SDK, or library. More on the timeline for developers is <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/preview/overview\">here</a>. </p> \n       <center> \n        <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-_fkqyA1NGXo/YKMO2EhX7YI/AAAAAAAAQiY/3RVCeKlJr8wFLRYYiBW_2EQNV5iq3lGHgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-12-desktop-timeline-en-may.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"timeline\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-_fkqyA1NGXo/YKMO2EhX7YI/AAAAAAAAQiY/3RVCeKlJr8wFLRYYiBW_2EQNV5iq3lGHgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-12-desktop-timeline-en-may.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n       </center> <h2><strong>Get started with Android 12!</strong></h2> <p> Today‚Äôs Beta release has everything you need to try the Android 12 features, test your apps, and give us <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/feedback\">feedback</a>. Just <a href=\"https://www.google.com/android/beta\">enroll any supported Pixel device here</a> to get the update over-the-air. If you‚Äôve already installed a preview build, you‚Äôll automatically get Beta updates. To get started developing, set up the SDK. </p> <p> You can also get Android 12 Beta on devices from some of our top device-maker partners who are participating in the Android 12 Developer Preview program. Visit <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/devices\">android.com/beta</a> to see the full list of partners, with links to their sites with details on their supported devices. Each partner will handle their own enrollments and support, and provide the Beta updates to you directly. </p> <p> For even broader testing on supported devices, try Android 12 Beta on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/gsi-release-notes\">Android GSI images</a>, and if you don‚Äôt have a device you can test on the Android Emulator -- just download the latest emulator system images via the SDK Manager in Android Studio. </p> <p> For complete details on how to get the Beta, visit the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/12\">Android 12 developer site</a>. </p> \n       <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n        <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=hGLAJopHf04:VV2LrZUyVRk:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"What's new in foldables, tablets, and large screens","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/_OVomqs6r0A/whats-new-in-foldables-tablets-and.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image \" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1fuLFiJuxIM/YKLms6qO9kI/AAAAAAAAAHc/f-5vyCClU_YxRB1wywMOYQdO1bDcsxL9ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image2.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1fuLFiJuxIM/YKLms6qO9kI/AAAAAAAAAHc/f-5vyCClU_YxRB1wywMOYQdO1bDcsxL9ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image2.png\" name=\"twitter:image\"> <p><em>Posted by Oscar Wahltinez, Developer Relations Engineer, Google</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0px; text-align: center;\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1000\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1fuLFiJuxIM/YKLms6qO9kI/AAAAAAAAAHc/f-5vyCClU_YxRB1wywMOYQdO1bDcsxL9ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image2.png\" /></a>\n     </div> \n    </center> <p> Users are seeing more value in larger screens, and the benefits of doing more with a single device. Apps designed for large screen devices increase those benefits even further. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"> <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Qkiz3QIPJzk\" title=\"YouTube video player\" width=\"560\"></iframe> </p> <p> The ability to fold a screen offers better ergonomics for large devices. When folded, you can fit a tablet-sized screen in your pocket ‚Äî unlocking utility that was previously unavailable on a portable device. Thinking about our app ecosystem, we‚Äôre excited because this is a hardware shift that is driving new expectations around what you can do from a handheld device. We see the demand for larger screens extending to tablets too, which have greatly increased in popularity, given the similar app experience. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EljZ5-h_wV4/YKLyZOhq4vI/AAAAAAAAAHk/AK8Rj3zjIbUA_ESW8cgF8hEXE1fKZ6YowCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image10.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Technological breakthroughs and our understanding of ergonomics have played a role in device form factors.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"231\" data-original-width=\"600\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EljZ5-h_wV4/YKLyZOhq4vI/AAAAAAAAAHk/AK8Rj3zjIbUA_ESW8cgF8hEXE1fKZ6YowCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image10.gif\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Technological breakthroughs and our understanding of ergonomics have played a role in device form factors.</em></p> <p> In this blog post, we'll explain what you should do to prepare your apps for large screens, and how recent updates have made developing your app easier. But first, let‚Äôs talk about what we're seeing with large screens ‚Äî and why you should optimize your app. </p> <h1>Why large screens</h1> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oR_4ZO51FIk/YKLy8VBLvCI/AAAAAAAAAHs/HtwHri_0f7oyLCDk7Wli_qDKaDgkAKFmQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image9.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"There are many ways to use foldable devices, including a number of postures\n  illustrated here.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"198\" data-original-width=\"871\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oR_4ZO51FIk/YKLy8VBLvCI/AAAAAAAAAHs/HtwHri_0f7oyLCDk7Wli_qDKaDgkAKFmQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image9.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>There are many ways to use foldable devices, including a number of postures illustrated here.</em></p> <p> Over the past year, we‚Äôve seen device makers release exciting new foldable and tablet devices. Demand has increased as users are doing more than ever from these devices. Altogether, developers can reach more than 250 million active foldables, tablets, and Chromebooks by building for Android large screen devices today. Sales of tablet devices grew 16% in 2020 with analysts expecting more than 400 million Android tablets by 2023, and foldables are redefining what‚Äôs possible on premium devices. Android apps can also run on ChromeOS, which is now the <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/technology-56116573\">second most popular</a> desktop OS. </p> <h1>Large screen ready</h1> <p> Larger screens are changing how users interact with their device. These devices allow you to edit slide decks while looking at notes, look up restaurant recommendations while planning a night out, or watch a video while chatting with friends. Let‚Äôs talk about base-level support ‚Äî features an app must support to be ‚Äúlarge screen ready‚Äù. There are three main areas of focus when it comes to large screen readiness: </p> \n    <ol> \n     <li>Designing for large screens</li> \n     <li>Multitasking</li> \n     <li>Input modes</li> \n    </ol> <p> They‚Äôre summarized below, but make sure to check out our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/docs/quality-guidelines/large-screens-app-quality\">large screen app quality guidelines</a> for the full details. </p> <h2>Design for large screens</h2> <p> The first step is to ensure that your app is designed for large screens. To make this easier, we‚Äôve defined specific window size breakpoints and device classes for you to optimize for. Add tablet layouts for displays where the shortest dimension is &gt;600dp, and ensure your apps <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/gestures/edge-to-edge\">go edge-to-edge</a>. Developers should also plan for their app to be used in both portrait and landscape modes, since larger screens are more likely to be used in landscape. We‚Äôve got material adaptive components that we‚Äôll be talking about to help developers make better use of the increased space. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lZoOir9Kkkc/YKLzqnG85II/AAAAAAAAAH0/Szu0jmG3rjIQWVSDpLEEPRKpRCd_GVMhgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image4.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Since foldable and large screen devices have a variable window size, adaptive\n  layouts work better than splitting experiences based on screen size.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"223\" data-original-width=\"927\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lZoOir9Kkkc/YKLzqnG85II/AAAAAAAAAH0/Szu0jmG3rjIQWVSDpLEEPRKpRCd_GVMhgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image4.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Since foldable and large screen devices have a variable window size, adaptive layouts work better than splitting experiences based on screen size.</em></p> <h2>Multitasking</h2> <p> Going into split screen (or multi-window mode) and gestures like drag and drop are starting to become natural interactions that users expect to work seamlessly in their large screen devices. Your apps should handle multitasking seamlessly by being resizable. Handling folding and unfolding events and planning for your app to be in multi-window mode prevents your app from becoming letterboxed. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EAjPyCQ3pdM/YKLz_P6FaWI/AAAAAAAAAH8/9v-B5fdxapM9g9BPP2Z00nSRM17S5TGbgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image12.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Drag and drop can be a natural interaction in large screen layouts, even within the same\n  app.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1500\" data-original-width=\"1500\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EAjPyCQ3pdM/YKLz_P6FaWI/AAAAAAAAAH8/9v-B5fdxapM9g9BPP2Z00nSRM17S5TGbgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image12.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/drag-drop\">Drag and drop</a> can be a natural interaction in large screen layouts, even within the same app.</em></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-m0AupDyjhf8/YKL0xrkwqWI/AAAAAAAAAIE/aZgAUPMWf24sq09gz180YPsQpkytnZnwgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"By enabling multiple instance support, users can run multiple copies of your\n  app side-by-side. The let‚Äôs users compare two products, reference notes\n  while writing a document or maybe keeping your calendar in view as you are\n  planning an event.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1182\" data-original-width=\"1320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-m0AupDyjhf8/YKL0xrkwqWI/AAAAAAAAAIE/aZgAUPMWf24sq09gz180YPsQpkytnZnwgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image6.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>By enabling multiple instance support, users can run multiple copies of your app side-by-side. The let‚Äôs users compare two products, reference notes while writing a document or maybe keeping your calendar in view as you are planning an event.</em></p> <h2>Input modes</h2> <p> Since many people use larger screens for productivity, tablets should support basic keyboard, mouse and stylus usage. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-d4lfGstDaK4/YKL1JO9nlhI/AAAAAAAAAIM/mD2TXCzRhXAWqehz1VtxsPLMGS_mPBYtACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image13.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Users of Android apps on ChromeOS devices often have a keyboard; apps should ensure that standard keyboard navigation and shortcuts are available to provide improved accessibility.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"515\" data-original-width=\"725\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-d4lfGstDaK4/YKL1JO9nlhI/AAAAAAAAAIM/mD2TXCzRhXAWqehz1VtxsPLMGS_mPBYtACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image13.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Users of Android apps on ChromeOS devices often have a keyboard; apps should ensure that standard keyboard navigation and shortcuts are available to provide improved accessibility.</em></p> <h1>Component updates</h1> <p> Several UI components across Jetpack and Material Design libraries have been updated to help you build a flexible user experience to scale your phone's UI to a larger screen. </p> <h2>SlidingPaneLayout</h2> <p> One of the most common adaptive layouts to optimize your app for large screens is implementing a list-detail UI. For example, a messaging app that lists messages on one side with the message detail on the other. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zU_VLtkAWrk/YKL12ZwrkaI/AAAAAAAAAIU/K2RQzY7bkmE66SD2SqGYvg9dVQvr7gTEgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image3.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"SlidingPaneLayout automatically adapts to configuration changes to provide a good user experience across different layout sizes.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"308\" data-original-width=\"542\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zU_VLtkAWrk/YKL12ZwrkaI/AAAAAAAAAIU/K2RQzY7bkmE66SD2SqGYvg9dVQvr7gTEgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image3.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em> SlidingPaneLayout automatically adapts to configuration changes to provide a good user experience across different layout sizes.</em></p> <p> UIs that would be one top of each other on a smaller screen can now easily lay out side-by-side. For this, you can use the updated version of the <code> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/slidingpanelayout\">SlidingPaneLayout</a> </code> library ‚Äî updated to support a two-pane style layout, <code> SlidingPaneLayout </code> uses the width of the two panes to determine how to lay out the UI. It does that by automatically determining if it can lay out side-by-side based on the content width and available space. For example, if the list pane is measured to have a minimum width of 200dp and the detail pane needs 400dp, then the <code> SlidingPaneLayout </code> automatically shows the two panes side by side if it has at least 600dp of width available. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jVqvDC29TXk/YKL2wyK_85I/AAAAAAAAAIc/aKeNhMyUnu8dnMjFk4ACmkx76_eAYf1qQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image1.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"SlidingPaneLayout is used in our sample application IOSched.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1164\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jVqvDC29TXk/YKL2wyK_85I/AAAAAAAAAIc/aKeNhMyUnu8dnMjFk4ACmkx76_eAYf1qQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image1.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>SlidingPaneLayout is used in our sample application <a href=\"https://github.com/google/iosched\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">IOSched</a>.</em></p> <p> We have updated the library to recognize and adapt to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/window/FoldingFeature\"> folds and hinges </a>. For example, if you are on a device with hinges that blocks part of the screen, it will automatically place your content on either side. </p> <p> We have also introduced <strong>lock modes</strong>,which allow control over the swipe behavior when panes overlap (programmatically switching is also supported). For example, to prevent users from swiping to an empty pane you may want them to have to click on a list item to load information about that pane, but allow them to swipe back to the list. On a foldable device or tablet that has room to show both views side by side, the lock modes are ignored. </p> <h2>NavRail</h2> <p> A <a href=\"https://material.io/components/navigation-rail\">vertical Navigation Rail</a> is functionally equivalent to Bottom navigation, and provides a more ergonomic navigation experience on larger screens. As you scale your UI, NavRail supports better reachability, since larger screens tend to be held by the side, whereas on the phone users are probably holding the device from the bottom. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RluQ9tduxbs/YKL3uOXZ2aI/AAAAAAAAAIk/3Y1vDPsVuzkEuGu5umggpgLn5zoYCZi-gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image11.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"NavRail automatically changes the location of the navigation menu depending\n\ton configuration changes.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"249\" data-original-width=\"281\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RluQ9tduxbs/YKL3uOXZ2aI/AAAAAAAAAIk/3Y1vDPsVuzkEuGu5umggpgLn5zoYCZi-gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image11.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>NavRail automatically changes the location of the navigation menu depending on configuration changes.</em></p> <p> For example, NavRail can help if vertical scrolling is key to your app. In those cases, a bottom navigation bar decreases the amount of content that‚Äôs visible, especially when tablet devices are being used in landscape orientation. </p> <h2>Other Components</h2> <p> We've also made updates across multiple other components. One of the biggest pitfalls when apps move to a larger screen is when UIs are stretched edge-to-edge across the whole screen. To help prevent this, we‚Äôve added default Max Width values to certain Material Components where this commonly happens, for example: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li>Buttons</li> \n     <li>TextFields</li> \n     <li>Sheets</li> \n    </ul> <p> We will add more components to this list in the future. These changes provide opinionated defaults to help your apps adapt and look better out of the box on large screen devices. Find more information about using size constraints with components in <a href=\"https://material.io/design/layout/component-behavior.html\">the Material Design guidelines</a>. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bMkfE5YJw9Q/YKL4MlVjJHI/AAAAAAAAAIs/AQCX18Hs2VUjzd2CMtz4i5-uQrK7Af4lQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image7.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:500px\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Most foreground UI elements should have a maximum width value.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1000\" data-original-width=\"871\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bMkfE5YJw9Q/YKL4MlVjJHI/AAAAAAAAAIs/AQCX18Hs2VUjzd2CMtz4i5-uQrK7Af4lQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image7.gif\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Most foreground UI elements should have a maximum width value.</em></p> <h2>WindowManager Jetpack library</h2> <p> Beyond component updates to help you scale your UI, we also have the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/window\">WindowManager Jetpack library</a> to help you build better experiences on these devices. This library is now available in alpha and it provides a common API surface for supporting different device types, starting with foldables and tablets. </p> <p> You can use WindowManager to detect display features such as folds or hinges. It also gives information about how the display feature affects your app, so you can create an optimal experience. For example, reacting to the foldable device state changes when the device is folded into tabletop mode while the user is watching a video. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-D2rVNrNhv4Q/YKL4nYihv2I/AAAAAAAAAI0/d6qRP4ye1FgpZfZ4gatV3FKVBDT0nSHAwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image5.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Applications should seamlessly adapt to a growing number of device configurations.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"441\" data-original-width=\"963\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-D2rVNrNhv4Q/YKL4nYihv2I/AAAAAAAAAI0/d6qRP4ye1FgpZfZ4gatV3FKVBDT0nSHAwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/image5.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Applications should seamlessly adapt to a growing number of device configurations.</em></p> <p> WindowManager also provides a couple of convenience methods to retrieve the current and maximum <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/window/WindowMetrics\">WindowMetrics</a> information in a backward compatible way, starting from API level 14. </p> <h1>Platform changes</h1> <h2>Display API deprecations</h2> <p> Your app needs to determine the screen or display size in order to render content appropriately for each device. With the introduction of the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/WindowMetrics\">WindowMetrics API</a>, a number of methods related to display size have been deprecated. For a backwards-compatible replacement, you should use the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/window\">Window Manager Jetpack library</a>. </p> <h2>Exclusive resources</h2> <p> Android 10 introduced the possibility to have multiple resumed apps running at the same time, with a single ‚Äútop resumed‚Äù application. Most applications benefit from this change without the need of updates. The most notable exception is if your application uses an exclusive resource like the microphone or the camera. See <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/android-at-large-how-to-bring-optimized-experiences-to-the-big-screen-a50a6784e59d\">our previous blog post</a> for more details. </p> <h1>Case studies</h1> <p> Optimizing your app for large screens can improve the experience for your users, as well as deliver on business results. We‚Äôre seeing an increased number of apps take advantage of the opportunities with large screens on Google Play. As an example, <a href=\"http://d.android.com/stories/apps/google-duo\">Google Duo</a> implemented tablet and foldable support to enhance their user experience, and saw an increase in app ratings and user engagement. </p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-G6tPgMmOEvY/YKPV-ivfZmI/AAAAAAAAQj0/YmvF29G4l5gqvqI5YHFGOn5CoMc1EDNIACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/LS_Before_After_Tabletop_cropped.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Google Duo's optimized experience for foldable devices\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1125\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-G6tPgMmOEvY/YKPV-ivfZmI/AAAAAAAAQj0/YmvF29G4l5gqvqI5YHFGOn5CoMc1EDNIACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/LS_Before_After_Tabletop_cropped.png\" /></a></p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\" id=\"imgCaption\"><em> Google Duo's optimized experience for foldable devices, such as the Samsung Galaxy Z Fold2 </em></p> <p> In addition to Google Duo's enhanced user experience, we've modernized many additional apps to use adaptive layouts so they can take advantage of large screens and foldable devices: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li>Chrome added improved tab navigation for larger screens</li> \n     <li>YouTube redesigned its UI to improve usability in foldable devices</li> \n     <li> Google Photos displays more UI elements, like a search bar, in larger screens </li> \n     <li>Google Developers like all of you are a crucial part of helping people stay connected while on the go. We‚Äôre seeing strong momentum across our in-car experiences, Android Auto and Android Automotive OS, and today, we‚Äôre excited to share the latest updates and opportunities to reach users in the car. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/FKaBhUue-nE\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Check out our I/O session: What's new with Android for Cars </p> <p> <h2>Android Auto </h2> </p> <p> <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/MDM4N1iA3NM/android.com/auto\">Android Auto</a>, which allows users to connect their phone to their car display, now has over 100 million compatible cars on the road and is supported by nearly every major car manufacturer. Porsche is our newest partner and they will begin shipping Android Auto on new cars, starting this summer with the Porsche 911. </p> <p> We‚Äôve been working closely with car manufacturers to build an even better Android Auto experience by enabling wireless projection in more vehicles, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Android/status/1376920861979123716\">extending availability to more countries</a>, and continuing to launch new features, like integration into the instrument cluster. To see some of the newest Android Auto technology in the BMW iX, check out the video below. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/BlIOyNvBaeQ\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Android Auto projecting to the cluster display in a BMW iX.</p> \n    </center> <p> <h2>Android Automotive OS</h2> </p> <p> Our newest in-car experience, <a href=\"https://source.android.com/devices/automotive/start/what_automotive\">Android Automotive OS</a> with Google apps and services built-in, also has strong momentum. With this experience, the entire infotainment system is powered by Android and users can access Google Assistant, Google Maps, and more apps from Google Play directly from the car screen without relying on a phone. Cars from Polestar and Volvo, like the Polestar 2 and the Volvo XC40 Recharge, are already available to customers. And by the end of 2021, this experience will be available to order in more than 10 car models from Volvo, General Motors and Renault. You can get a sneak peek of this customized experience in the new GMC HUMMER EV<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ktjBX1-1y-c\"> </a>below. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/ktjBX1-1y-c\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> The all-electric GMC HUMMER EV infotainment features Android Automotive OS with Google built-in. Preproduction model shown. Actual production models may vary. Initial availability Fall 2021. </p> \n    </center> <h2>Developing new apps for cars</h2> <p> To support this growing ecosystem, we recently made the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/android-auto-apps-powered-by-jetpack.html\">Android for Cars App Library available as part of Jetpack</a>. It allows developers of navigation, EV charging and parking apps to bring their apps to Android Auto compatible cars. Many of these developers have already <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/collection/promotion_apps_all_android_auto_on_the_go\">published their Android Auto apps to the Play Store</a> and we‚Äôre now extending this library to also support Android Automotive OS, making it easy for you to build once and generate apps that are compatible with both platforms. We‚Äôre already working with Early Access Partners ‚Äî including Parkwhiz, Plugshare, Sygic, ChargePoint, Flitsmeister, SpotHero and others ‚Äî to bring apps in these categories to cars powered by Android Automotive OS. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-xUxdeY6A8tA/YKLStyC1fcI/AAAAAAAAQgk/vzYCt_ayIKwDVnPInukBZpbV-HihsL8KwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/PlugShare.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android for cars\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-xUxdeY6A8tA/YKLStyC1fcI/AAAAAAAAQgk/vzYCt_ayIKwDVnPInukBZpbV-HihsL8KwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/PlugShare.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> PlugShare, an app for finding EV chargers, has used the Android for Cars App Library and Google Assistant App Actions to build for Android Auto. </p> \n    </center> <p> We plan to expand to more app categories in the future, so if you‚Äôre interested in joining our Early Access Program, please fill out <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/1qu-KzNZH260dbZlDSXEHMkd1iqm2fMv2AoFxPozeXgs/viewform?resourcekey=0-tLnNLS30DedMsLJKmVstfw&amp;edit_requested=true\">this interest form</a>. ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/48_y649MH8A/whats-new-in-google-play-2021.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" Google Play </em><p> <p> This year, we announced many great new features, tools, and updates to help you make the most of Google Play. You can check out all the updates in our I/O session, or keep reading for a quick overview of the new capabilities that will help take your business even further, from driving more installs to growing your engagement and revenue. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/tc57iyl06ww\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>15% service fee for the first $1M in earnings</h2> <p> 1. Earlier this year, we <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/boosting-dev-success.html\">announced</a> an additional service fee tier to help boost developer success on Google Play. Starting July 1st, the service fee will be 15% instead of 30% for your first $1M (USD) of earnings each year. You‚Äôll be able to enroll for the new rate in Play Console the week of June 7th, so we‚Äôre <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/10632485\">sharing details</a> about the process now to give you time to get ready. </p> <p> <h2>New tools for managing policy compliance</h2> </p> <p> 2. We‚Äôve built a new, dedicated Policy and Programs section in Play Console to provide you with a centralized place to see any policy compliance concerns, guidance on how to fix policy issues, and information about upcoming policy changes. </p> <p> <h2>More SDK guidance</h2> </p> <p> 3. The new Google Play SDK Console lets providers report issues with their SDK versions so we can give you better guidance and recommendations. We‚Äôve started with several large SDK providers and will continue to add more. </p> <p> 4. Later this year, we‚Äôre launching a new, public website with important insights about popular SDKs to help you choose the right SDK for your app. Learn more about how we‚Äôre helping you build safer and more stable apps in the I/O session below. \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/apHcQXxMUIs\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> <p> <h2>Helping more users discover your apps and games</h2> </p> <p> 5. To ensure that your store listing assets can help users anticipate your in-app or in-game experience and drive meaningful downloads, we‚Äôre <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/04/updated-guidance-to-improve-your-app.html\">pre-announcing a policy change</a> for app metadata... </p> <p> 6. and introducing <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/04/updated-guidance-to-improve-your-app.html\">new guidelines</a> on store listing preview assets. </p> <p> <h2>Distribution features for the future of publishing</h2> </p> <p> 7. One million apps are in production using the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/platform/technology/app-bundle\">Android App Bundle</a>, with 15% size savings on average vs a universal APK. The app bundle is the future of publishing on Google Play and, <strong>starting August 1, 2021, they‚Äôll be required for all new apps</strong>. </p> <p> 8. Based on developer feedback, we'll soon be launching an optional code transparency feature to offer additional cryptographic assurance that your app‚Äôs code on device has not been modified from its original version. </p> <p> <h2>Identify growth opportunities with our new competitive insights</h2> </p> <p> 9. To help you understand your <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/google-play-console-powers-better.html\">engagement and monetization trends</a> and optimize your product plans, we‚Äôve taken the best of our ecosystem data and contextualized your performance against peersets. Learn how to make the most of them in the I/O session below. </p> \n     <center> \n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/iBxYrEkpCac\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n     </center> <p> 10. You can now also customize and pin the precise metrics that matter to you in a <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/04/customize-kpis-on-your-google-play.html\">personalized KPIs section</a> at the top of your app dashboard. </p> <p> <h2>More features for a flexible monetization strategy</h2> </p> <p> 11. Your global reach just got even larger: In 2020, we added 34 new local forms of payment across 30 markets around the world. </p> <p> 12. We lowered the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/sub-dollar-pricing-expansion-in-20.html\">minimum prices</a> developers can set for paid apps, in-app purchases, and subscriptions in 20 new markets across Latin America, EMEA, and APAC. </p> <p> 13. This year, we‚Äôll be launching multi-quantity purchases, which will allow your users to buy more than one item at a time from the cart. </p> <p> 14. We‚Äôll also be launching multi-line subscriptions, which will allow you to sell multiple products as part of a single subscription. </p> <p> 15. And finally, we‚Äôll be launching prepaid plans, which will let you offer users access to content for a fixed amount of time. (Don‚Äôt worry, users can easily extend at any time.) </p> <p> 16. Want to take advantage of these new features? Many will be available when you integrate <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/48_y649MH8A/goo.gle/play-commerce\">Play Billing Library version 4.0</a>, and more will be rolling out later this year. As a reminder, <strong>new apps are required to integrate version 3.0 by August 2, 2021 or by November 1, 2021 for updates to existing apps</strong>. </p> <p> <h2>Program enhancements to engage and retain users</h2> </p> <p> 17. This year, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/googleplaypass/\">Google Play Pass</a> expanded to over 40 markets, with more than 800 games and apps. Developers have on average more than doubled their Play revenue across participating titles in these markets. <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSdmL0YkKrklqZHTcb6sVZLnSXA7Tf5TELppa0mx7tAn1x3AJA/viewform\">Let us know if you‚Äôd like to join</a>! </p> <p> 18. Google Play Points expanded to 22 countries and added deeper integration with Play Console making it even easier for developers to onboard. Play‚Äôs loyalty program helps developers increase engagement and reduce churn with their most high value users. <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/googleplaypoints\">Developers can learn more about joining the program here.</a> </p> <p> <h2>More educational content</h2> </p> <p> 19. Want to learn more about any of these features? We‚Äôve built a <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/\">comprehensive website</a> with best practices and resources to help you learn more about our programs and tools. </p> <p> 20. Last but not least, we‚Äôve also added tons of new free courses to <a href=\"https://play.google.com/academy/\">Google Play Academy</a>. Whether you're about to launch your startup or grow your existing business on Play, Google Play Academy has you covered. \n      <center> \n       <p> How useful did you find this blog post? </p> \n 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"What‚Äôs new in Android Privacy","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/Ulzl5Vg5bWA/android-security-and-privacy-recap.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4p_wvqXkDhg/YKMSkzlZCZI/AAAAAAAAQis/vWgHdB-a3U4syecmyO0O3zuBr3u3t5wVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android_SecurityAndPrivacy_1024x512-01_Updated%2B%25281%2529.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4p_wvqXkDhg/YKMSkzlZCZI/AAAAAAAAQis/vWgHdB-a3U4syecmyO0O3zuBr3u3t5wVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android_SecurityAndPrivacy_1024x512-01_Updated%2B%25281%2529.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Sara N-Marandi, Product Manager, Android Platform Product</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4p_wvqXkDhg/YKMSkzlZCZI/AAAAAAAAQis/vWgHdB-a3U4syecmyO0O3zuBr3u3t5wVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android_SecurityAndPrivacy_1024x512-01_Updated%2B%25281%2529.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android privacy\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4p_wvqXkDhg/YKMSkzlZCZI/AAAAAAAAQis/vWgHdB-a3U4syecmyO0O3zuBr3u3t5wVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Android_SecurityAndPrivacy_1024x512-01_Updated%2B%25281%2529.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> People want an OS and apps that they can trust with their most personal and sensitive information. Privacy is core to Android‚Äôs product principles. As shared in the ‚Äú<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gTUt9mwfPS8\">What‚Äôs new in Android Privacy</a>‚Äù session, Android 12 continues to expand on this existing foundation by making the platform even more private. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/gTUt9mwfPS8\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> This release will give users more transparency around the data being accessed by apps while providing simple controls to make informed choices. Android is also investing in reducing the scope of permissions so that apps only have access to the data they need for the features they provide. Let‚Äôs look at some of these important changes we‚Äôve made in Android 12 to protect user privacy. </p> <p> <strong>Privacy dashboard: </strong>Users often tell us that they want to understand what data apps use. With the new Privacy Dashboard, users will have a simple and clear timeline view of the last 24 hour accesses to location, microphone and camera. You can also share more context about your app‚Äôs data usage with a new permission intent API in Android 12. The Privacy dashboard will be available to try in Beta 2. </p> <p> We encourage all developers to review your code and understand data access needs, including those in third-party SDKs, and make sure all accesses have justifiable use cases. To help with that, in Android 11 we added <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/data/audit-access\">Data access auditing APIs</a> to make it easy for you to audit your current data access. Use the APIs to untangle mapping of your code by tracking which part of your code accesses private data. The Privacy dashboard will be available to try in Beta 2. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/Ulzl5Vg5bWA/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--U1ovcwneck/YKMTTeJGHeI/AAAAAAAAQi0/tESBgovjzdMAfupStekIArK5PNGQN_zhwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.gif \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Privacy dashboard and location access timeline\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--U1ovcwneck/YKMTTeJGHeI/AAAAAAAAQi0/tESBgovjzdMAfupStekIArK5PNGQN_zhwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Figure 1. Privacy dashboard and location access timeline in the past 24 hours. </p> \n    </center> <p> <strong>Microphone and camera indicators: </strong>In Android 12 we‚Äôre adding transparency to microphone and camera access. Going forward, users will know in real time when an app accesses their microphone or camera feeds. By simply going into Quick Settings, users can view the apps accessing their data. If the access is unwarranted, users can quickly navigate to the app permission page to revoke permissions. </p> <p> Developers should review their use of microphone and camera and proactively remove unexpected access. For example, you should ensure that your app does not access these sensors before the user clicks on a feature that needs access. The Microphone and camera indicators will be available to try in Beta 2. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HuzH3M099T8/YKMT_0J0YfI/AAAAAAAAQi8/bDBojBs97A0_xAzIgUWh0jzXKEUDa2cuACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled%2B%25281%2529.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\" Microphone and camera indicators and toggles\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HuzH3M099T8/YKMT_0J0YfI/AAAAAAAAQi8/bDBojBs97A0_xAzIgUWh0jzXKEUDa2cuACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled%2B%25281%2529.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Figure 2. Microphone and camera indicators and toggles. </p> \n    </center> <p> <strong>Microphone and camera toggles: </strong>You may have seen people placing stickers on cameras or plugging audio blockers into their phones. In Android 12, we‚Äôre introducing two new controls that allow users to quickly and easily cut off apps‚Äô access to the microphone and camera on the device. To ensure user safety, emergency calls will be exempted. </p> <p> If an app with permissions attempts to access the microphone or camera but the user has the sensors turned off, the system will display a message to inform the user that they must turn the sensors back on in order to use the app‚Äôs features. If your app follows <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/permissions/usage-notes\">permissions best practices</a>, then you don‚Äôt need to do anything different to incorporate the toggle state. The Microphone and camera toggles will be available to try in Beta 2. </p> <p> <strong>Approximate location:</strong> Over the last two releases, we‚Äôve made location permission fine grained. First, we separated background and foreground access. Then, we added an ‚Äúonly this time‚Äù option to further restrict access to background location. We‚Äôre seeing users respond positively to these controls and are choosing them more often. When given the option, users elect to share less through foreground location access about 80% of the time. </p> <p> In Android 12, we will give users more control over their location data. Users will have a clear choice regarding the precision of location provided to the app by selecting approximate location. </p> <p> We encourage you to review your use case for location and request <code> ACCESS_COARSE_LOCATION </code> if your features don‚Äôt need the user‚Äôs precise location. You should also be prepared for users to reduce location precision. Please make sure your app still works when users select approximate. Approximate location will be available to try in Beta 1. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/Ulzl5Vg5bWA/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-98jX3g1mzEo/YKMUgriePUI/AAAAAAAAQjE/mzlpynZb4V8LMPqywuph3rbjyvfVxQTvQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled%2B%25282%2529.gif \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Location permission request dialog with approximate and precise selection\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-98jX3g1mzEo/YKMUgriePUI/AAAAAAAAQjE/mzlpynZb4V8LMPqywuph3rbjyvfVxQTvQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled%2B%25282%2529.gif \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Figure 3. Location permission request dialog with approximate and precise selection </p> <p> <strong>Clipboard read notification: </strong>Content copied to the clipboard can contain sensitive information as users frequently copy emails, addresses, and even passwords. Android 12 notifies users every time an app reads from their clipboard. Users will see a toast at the bottom of the screen each time an app calls <code> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/ClipboardManager#getPrimaryClip%28%29\">getPrimaryClip()</a> </code> . The toast won‚Äôt appear if clipboard data originates from the same app. You can minimize access by first checking <code> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/ClipboardManager#getPrimaryClipDescription%28%29\">getPrimaryClipDescription()</a></code> to learn about the type of data in the clipboard. The recommended best practice is to only access the clipboard when the user understands why the access occured. Clipboard read notification will be available to try in Beta 2. </p> <p> <strong>Nearby device permissions: </strong>Android 12 minimizes data access by adding a new runtime permission for nearby experiences that do not use location. Up until now, apps such as watch and headphone companion apps required the location permission to scan for nearby Bluetooth devices for pairing. We heard from users and developers that this was confusing and led to granting the permission to access location data when it wasn‚Äôt needed. For apps targeting Android 12, you‚Äôll have the option to decouple nearby device discovery from the fine location permission for use cases like pairing devices by using the new <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission.html#BLUETOOTH_SCAN\"> BLUETOOTH_SCAN</a> </code> permission and by declaring <code> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/R.attr.html#usesPermissionFlags\">usesPermissionFlags=neverForLocation</a> </code>. Once the device is paired, apps can use the new <code> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission.html#BLUETOOTH_CONNECT\">BLUETOOTH_CONNECT</a> </code> permission to interact with it. Apps that use Bluetooth scanning for location must still have the location permission. Nearby device permissions will be available to try in Beta 1. </p> <p> <strong>App hibernation: </strong>Last year we launched <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/11/privacy/permissions#auto-reset\">permissions auto-reset</a>. If an app isn‚Äôt used for an extended period of time, Android automatically revokes permissions for the app. In the last 14 days permissions were reset for 8.5M apps. This year we‚Äôre building on permissions auto-reset by intelligently hibernating apps that have gone unused for an extended period - optimizing for device storage, performance and safety. The system not only revokes permissions granted previously by the user, but it also force-stops the app and reclaims memory, storage and other temporary resources. Users can bring apps out of hibernation simply by launching the app. App hibernation will be available to try in Beta 1. </p> <p> Android 12 is our most ambitious privacy release to date. Along the way, we have engaged closely with our developer community to build a platform that puts privacy at the forefront while taking into consideration the impact on developers. We thank you for your continued feedback and support in making our platform private and safe for everyone. Learn more about these changes on the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/behavior-changes-12#privacy\">developer site</a>. </p> \n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a
