":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn64@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-51-254_92de000dfb2a3323.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn17@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-44-600_e6aa4d73b74f71ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=Ulzl5Vg5bWA:I6_c2RXGKrI:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn67@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-45-118_d6e7d5751f828fa8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~4/Ulzl5Vg5bWA":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436143700},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"Mercari improves UI development productivity by 56% with Jetpack Compose","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/tt9_NWj8E4o/mercari-improves-ui-development.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\" https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YGhph7EgqT8/YKMbWIAO4UI/AAAAAAAAQjM/nOffYqFRx-8n6Sc7uUk1fpmqpFEHUf9egCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/BlogHeader_Android.jpg \"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YGhph7EgqT8/YKMbWIAO4UI/AAAAAAAAQjM/nOffYqFRx-8n6Sc7uUk1fpmqpFEHUf9egCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/BlogHeader_Android.jpg \"> <p><em>Posted by Chiko Shimizu, Partner Developer Advocate and Tamao Imura, Developer Marketing Manager </em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YGhph7EgqT8/YKMbWIAO4UI/AAAAAAAAQjM/nOffYqFRx-8n6Sc7uUk1fpmqpFEHUf9egCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/BlogHeader_Android.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Mercari improves UI development productivity by 56% with Jetpack Compose\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-YGhph7EgqT8/YKMbWIAO4UI/AAAAAAAAQjM/nOffYqFRx-8n6Sc7uUk1fpmqpFEHUf9egCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/BlogHeader_Android.jpg\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.kouzoh.mercari\">Mercari</a> allows millions of people to shop and sell almost anything. The company was founded in 2013 in Japan, and it now is the largest smartphone-focused C2C marketplace in Japan. Mercari‚Äôs Client Architect Team started using <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a> in 2020 with the goal of using modern solutions and technologies that can scale for the long term to build their tech stack for new applications. </p> <h2>What they did</h2> <p> The Mercari team needed to implement a design system with complex state management and styling on Android Views ‚Äî a very complex task. Using Jetpack Compose, they were not only able to implement this complex system, it helped them spend less time developing each screen. </p> <p> Jetpack Compose also helped the team write UI code for their new app utilizing the design system, making their UI code concise and easy to understand. As a result, the team can spend more time writing screens and business logic, such as practical support for the dark theme. </p> <p> In addition, the Mercari team wrote a proof-of-concept tool for integrating Figma with the design system, which automatically generates UI code from the component designs. The team said that developing this tool was easier with Compose due to its declarative nature. </p> <p> <em>‚ÄúOnce Android developers get used to writing Jetpack Compose code, they wouldn‚Äôt wish to go back.‚Äù - Anthony Allan Conda, Android Tech Lead at Mercari </em> </p> <h2>Results</h2> <p> Between Jetpack Compose and their new design system, Mercari was able to use far less code to write screens. On screens with infinitely-scrollable content ‚Äî a common use case ‚Äî they actually reduced their code by about 56%. As a result, they were able to write more screens in the same amount of time, giving them more time to write business logic and other parts of the code. </p> <p> Also, they were able to do more with the UI itself, such as incorporating animations and using intuitive APIs such as <em>AnimatedVisibility</em>, <em>Crossfade</em>, and <em>Animatable</em>. </p> <p> Mercari is planning to continue using Jetpack Compose in their new application until its release. Their design system, with the Android SDK written in Jetpack Compose, is also designed to work with multiple applications within Mercari. </p> <h2>Get started</h2> <p> Learn more about <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a>. </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a Director, Product Management &amp; Jacob Lehrbaum, Director of Developer Relations, Android &amp; Play </em><p> <p> As Android developers, we are all driven by building experiences that delight people around the world. And with people depending on your apps more than ever, expectations are higher and your jobs as developers aren‚Äôt getting easier. Today, at <a href=\"https://events.google.com/io/?lng=en\">Google I/O</a>, we covered a few ways that we‚Äôre trying to help out, whether it be through <strong>Android 12</strong> - one of the biggest design changes ever, Jetpack, Jetpack Compose, Android Studio, and Kotlin to <strong>help you build beautiful high quality apps</strong>. We‚Äôre also helping when it comes to extending your apps wherever your users go, like through <strong>wearables and larger-screened devices</strong>. You can watch the <a href=\"https://events.google.com/io/session/52ad33ce-1363-411e-bfdc-41250e2fa9bc?lng=en\">full Developer Keynote</a>, but here are a few highlights: </p> <p> <h2>Android 12: one of the biggest design updates ever. </h2> </p> <p> The first Beta of <a href=\"http://d.android.com/12\">Android 12</a> just started rolling out, and it‚Äôs packed with lots of cool stuff. From new user safety features like permissions for bluetooth and approximate location, enhancements to performance like expedited jobs and start up animations, to delightful experiences with more interactive widgets and stretch overscrolling, this release is one of the biggest design updates to Android ever. You can <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/android-12-beta-1.html\">read more about what‚Äôs in Android 12 Beta 1 here</a>, so you can start preparing your apps for the consumer release coming out later this year. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12\">Download the Beta</a> and try it with your apps today! </p> <p> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/7BP9yIf-HTc/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-73nbn4r0Imk/YKMtQF8ZPlI/AAAAAAAAQjs/TzvtHpXiFNcQJUM-ltLvyFRv7ezLwpWugCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.jpeg  \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android 12 visual\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-73nbn4r0Imk/YKMtQF8ZPlI/AAAAAAAAQjs/TzvtHpXiFNcQJUM-ltLvyFRv7ezLwpWugCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Untitled.jpeg \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     </center> </p> <p> <h2>Jetpack Compose: get ready for 1.0 in July! </h2> </p> <p> For the last few years, we‚Äôve been hard at work modernizing the Android development experience, listening to your feedback to keep the openness‚Äìa hallmark of Android, but becoming more opinionated about the right way to do things. You can see this throughout, from Android Studio, a performant IDE that can keep up with you, to Kotlin, a programming language that enables you to do more with less code, to Jetpack libraries that solve the hardest problems on mobile with backward compatibility. </p> <p> The next step in this offering is <a href=\"http://d.android.com/Compose\">Jetpack Compose</a> - our modern UI toolkit to easily build beautiful apps for all Android devices. We announced Compose here at Google I/O two years ago and since then have been building it in the open, listening to your feedback to make sure we got it right. With the Compose Beta earlier this year, developers around the world have created some truly beautiful, innovative experiences <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/mercari-improves-ui-development.html \">in half the time</a>, and the response to the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/androiddevchallenge-its-wrap.html\">#AndroidDevChallenge</a> blew our socks off! </p> <p> With the forthcoming update of Material You (which <a href=\"https://material.io/blog/announcing-material-you\">you can read more about here</a>), we‚Äôll be adding new Material components as well as further support for building for large screens, making it fast and easy to build a gorgeous UI. We‚Äôre pressure testing the final bits in Compose and will release 1.0 Stable in July‚Äîso get ready! </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/9AAmOcgdA2s\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> <h2>Android Studio Arctic Fox: Design, Devices, &amp; Developer Productivity! </h2> </p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio\">Android Studio</a> Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta, the latest release of the official powerful Android IDE, is out today to help you build quality apps easier and faster. We have delivered and updated the suite of tools to empower three major themes: accelerate your UI design, extend your app to new devices, and boost your developer productivity. With this latest release you can create modern UIs with Compose tooling, see test results across multiple devices, and optimize debugging databases and background tasks with the App Inspector. We‚Äôre also making your apps more accessible with the Accessibility Scanner and more performant with Memory Profiler. And for faster build speeds, we have the Android Gradle plugin 7.0, new DSL, and variant APIs. You can learn <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/android-studio-arctic-fox-beta.html\">more about the Android Studio updates here</a>. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NsTkrrFxpck/YKMrRS-FztI/AAAAAAAAQjU/WrTD3H36zMQ8Un6SSbKWan3fJvLFFCH0gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/StudioGif.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android Studio Arctic Fox\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NsTkrrFxpck/YKMrRS-FztI/AAAAAAAAQjU/WrTD3H36zMQ8Un6SSbKWan3fJvLFFCH0gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/StudioGif.gif\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> <h2>Kotlin: the most used language by professional Android devs</h2> </p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin\">Kotlin</a> is now the most used primary language by professional Android developers according to our recent surveys; in fact, over 1.2M apps in the Play Store use Kotlin, including 80% of the top 1000 apps. And here at Google, we love it too: 70+ Google apps like Drive, Home, Maps and Play use Kotlin. And with a brand-new native solution to annotation processing for Kotlin built from the ground up, Kotlin Symbol Processing is available today, a powerful and yet simple API for parsing Kotlin code directly, showing speeds up to 2x faster with libraries like Room. </p> <p> <h2>Android Jetpack: write features, not boilerplate </h2> </p> <p> With <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack\">Android Jetpack</a>, we built a suite of libraries to help reduce boilerplate code so you can focus on the code you care about. Over 84% of the top 10,000 apps are now using a Jetpack library. And today, we‚Äôre unpacking some new releases for Jetpack, including Jetpack Macrobenchmark (Alpha) to capture large interactions that affect your app startup and jank before your app is released, as well as a new Kotlin Coroutines API for persisting data more efficiently via Jetpack DataStore (Beta). You can <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/whats-new-in-jetpack.html\">read about all the updates in Android Jetpack here</a>. </p> <h2>Now is the time: a big step for Wear </h2> <p> The best thing about modern Android development is that these tools have been purpose built to help make it easy for you to build for the next era of Android, which is all about enabling devices connected to your phone‚ÄìTVs, cars, watches, tablets‚Äìto work better together. </p> <p> Starting today, we take <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/wear\">a huge step forward with wearables</a>. First, we introduced a unified platform built jointly with Samsung, combining the best of Wear and Tizen. Second, we shared a new consumer experience with revamped Google apps. And third, a world-class health and fitness service from Fitbit is coming to the platform. As an Android developer, it means you‚Äôll have more reach, and you‚Äôll be able to use all of your existing skills, tools, and APIs that make your mobile apps great, to build for a single wearables platform used by people all over the world. </p> <p> Whether it‚Äôs new Jetpack APIs for Wear tailored for small screens and designed to optimize battery life, to the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/articles/wear-tiles\">Jetpack Tiles API</a>, so you can create a custom Tile for all the devices in the Wear ecosystem, there are a number of new features to help you build on Wear. And with a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/health-services\">new set of APIs for Health and Fitness</a>, created in collaboration with Samsung, data collection from sensors and metrics computation is streamlined, consistent, and accurate‚Äìlike heart rate to calories to daily distance‚Äìfrom one trusted source. All this comes together in new tooling, with the release of Android Studio Arctic Fox Beta, like easier pairing to test apps, and even a virtual heart rate sensor in the emulator. And when your app is ready, users will have a much easier time discovering the world of Wear apps on Google Play, with some big updates to discoverability. You can <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/wear-os-at-io.html  \">read more about all of the Wear updates here</a>. </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/URx8_ZRR7ls\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> <h2>Tapping the momentum of larger screens, like tablets, Chrome OS and foldables</h2> </p> <p> When it comes to larger screens -- tablets, foldables, and Chrome OS laptops-- there is huge momentum. People are increasingly relying on large screen devices to stay connected with family and friends, go to school, or work remotely. In fact, there are over 250 million active large screen Android devices. Last year, Chrome OS grew +92% year over year‚Äì5 times the rate of the PC market, making Chrome OS the fastest growing and the second-most popular desktop OS. To help you take advantage of this momentum, we‚Äôre giving you APIs and tools to make optimizing that experience easier: like having your content resize automatically to more space by using <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/slidingpanelayout#1.2.0-alpha02\">SlidingpaneLayout 1.2.0 </a>and a new vertical navigation rail component, Max widths on components to avoid stretched UIs, as well as updates to the platform, Chrome OS, and Jetpack windowmanager, so apps work better by default. <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/whats-new-in-foldables-tablets-and.html\">You can learn more here</a>. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/7BP9yIf-HTc/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lCV9hv82PwI/YKMr5noyVpI/AAAAAAAAQjc/mKzieJLkumwJPwVp-psyuSnzGlTASlTXwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/unnamed%2B%25281%2529.png \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Google Duo's optimized experience for foldable devices\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-lCV9hv82PwI/YKMr5noyVpI/AAAAAAAAQjc/mKzieJLkumwJPwVp-psyuSnzGlTASlTXwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/unnamed%2B%25281%2529.png \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/stories/apps/google-duo?hl=en\">Google Duo's</a> optimized experience for foldable devices </p> \n    </center> <p> This is just a taste of some of the new ways we‚Äôre making it easier for you to build high quality Android apps. Later today, we‚Äôll be releasing more than 20 technical sessions on Android and Play, covering a wide range of topics such as background tasks, privacy, and Machine Learning on Android, or the top 12 tips to get you ready for Android 12. If building for cars, TVs, and wearables is your thing, we got that covered, too. You can find all these sessions - and more - on <a href=\"https://events.google.com/io/program/content?4=topic_android&amp;lng=en\">the I/O website</a>. You can check out the Android dome in <a href=\"http://g.co/io/adventure\">I/O Adventure</a>, where you can see new blog posts, videos, codelabs, and more. ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn66@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-44-566_73cf006703c42962.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn17@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-44-600_e6aa4d73b74f71ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=7BP9yIf-HTc:XwrKQqL0FPE:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn74@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-44-614_c782b5062c2c5e19.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~4/7BP9yIf-HTc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn67@2020_1/2021/05/19/14-56-45-598_3a0550aae3ecc568.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436143700},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"What's new in Jetpack","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/t5nL9K4vNFg/whats-new-in-jetpack.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4G4zVhAxueg/YKLth6HiL_I/AAAAAAAAQhM/JiTsOudkdXgb94qpNYI66jEGlauS0CETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-whats-new-in-jetpack-v2.png\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4G4zVhAxueg/YKLth6HiL_I/AAAAAAAAQhM/JiTsOudkdXgb94qpNYI66jEGlauS0CETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-whats-new-in-jetpack-v2.png\"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/fmuntenescu?lang=en\"> Florina Muntenescu</a>, Android Developer Advocate</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4G4zVhAxueg/YKLth6HiL_I/AAAAAAAAQhM/JiTsOudkdXgb94qpNYI66jEGlauS0CETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-whats-new-in-jetpack-v2.png \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"what's new in jetpack image\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4G4zVhAxueg/YKLth6HiL_I/AAAAAAAAQhM/JiTsOudkdXgb94qpNYI66jEGlauS0CETQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-whats-new-in-jetpack-v2.png \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> Android Jetpack is a suite of libraries, tools, and guidance to help developers follow best practices, reduce boilerplate code, and write code that works consistently across Android versions and devices. Today, 84% of the top 1000 apps on Google Play rely on Jetpack. </p> <p> Here‚Äôs a round-up of the latest updates in Jetpack - an extended version of our <em>What‚Äôs new in Jetpack</em> talk! </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/xeQ9faYJktM\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>New in Stable</h2> <strong>CameraX</strong> <p> The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/camerax\">CameraX</a> library provides a unified API surface for accessing camera functionality across OS versions, including device-specific compatibility fixes and workarounds. Some of the latest improvements to the library address common feature requests, including support for adjusting exposure compensation and access to more detailed information about camera state and features. Additionally, camera settings like FPS range can now be changed via <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/camera/camera2/interop/Camera2Interop\">Camera2Interop</a></code> while the camera is running. The library also brings support for the latest device and OS features, including high-dynamic-range preview, zoom ratio controls, and support for Android‚Äôs Do Not Disturb mode. Perhaps most importantly, though, the library has continued to address performance, resulting in faster image capture and faster initialization, especially on older devices. </p> <strong>Hilt</strong> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/dependency-injection/hilt-android?hl=en\">Hilt</a> is Jetpack‚Äôs recommended dependency injection solution built on top of Dagger. As part of the transition to stable, Hilt‚Äôs <code>ViewModel</code> support has moved up into the core Hilt Android APIs and <code>SavedStateHandle</code> has been added as a default dependency available in the <code>ViewModelComponent</code>. Also, Hilt is now integrated with Navigation and Compose: you can obtain an annotated Hilt ViewModel that is scoped to a destination or the navigation graph itself. Developers have already started using Hilt in their apps. Read about their experience in <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/hilt-is-stable-easier-dependency-injection-on-android-53aca3f38b9c\">this blog post</a>. </p> <strong>Paging 3.0</strong> <p> The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/architecture/paging/v3-overview?hl=en\">Paging</a> library allows you to load and display small chunks of data to improve </p> <p> network and system resource consumption. This release features a complete rewrite in Kotlin with first-class support for coroutines and Flow, asynchronous loading with RxJava and Guava primitives, and overall improvements to the repository and presentation layers. </p> <p> The 3.0 release is a substantial improvement in usability over Paging 2, and the rewrite was planned with partial and staged migrations in mind so that developers can transition on their own schedules. Check out the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/architecture/paging/v3-overview\">Paging 3.0 documentation</a> and the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/codelabs/android-paging#0\">Paging 3.0 codelab</a> for details and hands-on experience. </p> <strong>ConstraintLayout and MotionLayout</strong> <p> <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/constraint-layout?hl=en\">ConstraintLayout</a></code>, Jetpack‚Äôs flexible system for designing layouts, and <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/constraint-layout/motionlayout?hl=en\">MotionLayout</a></code>, an API aimed at managing motion and widget animation, are now stable. <code>MotionLayout</code> now includes support for foldable devices, image filters, and motion effects. To find out more about what‚Äôs new in design tools, check out <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/t5nL9K4vNFg/ https://youtu.be/B1u7JZ1rLyE\">this Google I/O talk</a>. </p> <strong>Security Crypto</strong> <p> The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/security/data\">Security Crypto</a> library allows you to safely and easily encrypt files and <code>SharedPreferences</code>. To encrypt <code>SharedPreferences</code>, create an <code>EncryptedSharedPreferences</code> object with the appropriate key and scheme and then use it like a standard SharedPreferences object. </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">val prefs: SharedPreferences = EncryptedSharedPreferences.create(\n        context,\n        \"prefs_file_name\",\n        mainKey,\n        prefKeyEncryptionScheme = AES256_SIV,\n        prefValueEncryptionScheme = AES256_GCM,\n)\n// Use the resulting SharedPreferences object as usual.\nprefs.edit()\n    .putBoolean(\"show_completed\", true)\n    .apply()</pre> <strong>Fragment</strong> <p> Over the past year, the Fragment library has undergone a major effort to clean up its internal implementation and reduce undocumented behavior, making it easier for developers to follow best practices in their apps and write reliable tests. This lays the groundwork for future improvements to the library, like supporting multiple back stacks in Navigation, and it may require some work to accommodate strict enforcement of API contracts. In practice, you should pay careful attention to your tests after updating the library. Check out the Fragment <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/fragment\">release notes</a> to see specific cases to watch out for. </p> <p> Recent releases have also introduced <code>ActivityResult</code> integration, making it possible to register for <code>Activity</code> results from a fragment. Fragment has also added a new <code>FragmentOnAttachListener</code> interface to replace the less-flexible <code>onAttachFragment</code> method. Existing code that overrides this method in <code>Fragment</code> or <code>FragmentActivity</code> will still work, but we‚Äôve deprecated <code>onAttachFragment</code> to help prevent new code from accidentally adopting a less-flexible approach. </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Obtain the fragment manager. May be a childFragmentManager,\n// if in a fragment, to observe child attachment.\nval fm = supportFragmentManager\n\nval listener = FragmentOnAttachListener {\n    fragmentManager, fragment -&gt;\n  // Respond to the fragment being attached.\n}\n\nfm.addFragmentOnAttachListener(listener)</pre> <h2>New in Beta</h2> <p> Once a library is feature complete it moves to Beta for stabilization. At this moment, the APIs change only in response to <strong>critical</strong> issues or community feedback. </p> <strong>DataStore</strong> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/architecture/datastore\">DataStore</a> provides a robust data storage solution that addresses the shortcomings of SharedPreferences while maintaining a simple, highly usable API surface. DataStore brings support for best practices like Kotlin coroutines with Flow and RxJava. DataStore allows you to store key-value pairs, via Preference DataStore or typed objects backed by protocol buffers, via Proto DataStore. You can also <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/using-datastore-with-kotlin-serialization-6552502c5345\">plug in</a> your own serialization solution, like Kotlin Serialization. </p> <p> </p> <h2>New in Alpha</h2> <p> Alpha libraries are libraries under active development‚ÄîAPIs may be added, changed, or removed, but what‚Äôs in the library is tested and should be highly functional. </p> <strong>AppSearch</strong> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/search/appsearch\">AppSearch</a> is a new on-device search library which provides high performance and feature-rich full-text search functionality. Compared to SQLite, AppSearch supports multiple world languages, simplifies ranking query results, and offers lower latency for indexing and searching over large datasets. </p> <p> AppSearch 1.0.0-alpha01 is released with LocalStorage support, which allows your application to manage structured data, called ‚Äúdocuments‚Äù, and then query over it. Your application defines what the structure looks like using ‚Äúschema types‚Äù. For instance, you can model a Message as a schema type with data such as subject, body, and sender. </p> <p> Use builders to create documents of a schema type and then add them to storage. Querying for ‚Äúbody:fruit‚Äù will retrieve all documents with the term ‚Äúfruit‚Äù in the body of the Message. </p> <p> In Android S, AppSearch will also offer PlatformStorage so you can share your application‚Äôs data with other applications securely, and reduce your application‚Äôs binary size by not having to link additional native libraries. This is currently not available in Jetpack because the library doesn‚Äôt target the Android S SDK yet. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RQrn4St_wGk/YKLrxCTi9yI/AAAAAAAAQg8/v3Sgr9aE9pw9UuvyWaDdHMxOaQ_CwUChwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-04-21%2Bat%2B10.39.07.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:400px\" alt=\"Centralized storage on Android S+ for integrating into device-wide search\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RQrn4St_wGk/YKLrxCTi9yI/AAAAAAAAQg8/v3Sgr9aE9pw9UuvyWaDdHMxOaQ_CwUChwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Screen%2BShot%2B2021-04-21%2Bat%2B10.39.07.png\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Centralized storage on Android S+ for integrating into device-wide search </p> \n    </center> <strong>Room</strong> <p> Room is the recommended data persistence layer, providing increased usability and safety over the platform. </p> <p> Room 2.4.0-alpha brings support for <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/room-auto-migrations-d5370b0ca6eb\">auto-migrations</a>. When your database schema changes, you now declare an <code>@AutoMigration</code> and indicate from which version to which version you want to migrate, and Room generates the migrations for you. For more complex migrations, you can still use the <code>Migration</code> class: </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">@Database(\n-   version = 1,\n+   version = 2,\n    entities = { Doggos.class },\n+   autoMigrations = {\n+         @AutoMigration (from = 1, to = 2)\n+     }\n  )\npublic abstract class DoggosDatabase extends RoomDatabase { }</pre> <p> Room 2.3.0 stable version brings experimental support for <a href=\"https://github.com/google/ksp\">Kotlin Symbol Processing</a> which, in our benchmarks of Kotlin code showed a 2x speed improvement over KAPT, as well as built-in support for enums and RxJava3. </p> <p> Room has also introduced a <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/androidx/room/RoomDatabase.QueryCallback\">QueryCallback</a></code> class‚Äîwhich provides a callback when SQLite statements are executed, to simplify tasks like logging‚Äîas well as the new <code>@ProvidedTypeConverter</code> annotation, which allows more flexibility when creating type converters. </p> <strong>WorkManager</strong> <p> The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/architecture/workmanager\">WorkManager</a> library‚ÄîAndroid‚Äôs recommended way to schedule deferrable, asynchronous tasks that run even if the app exits or the device restarts‚Äîhas made improvements to reliability with task reconciliation, ensuring all tasks are executed, and a variety of workarounds for specific Android OS versions. </p> <p> The latest versions of WorkManager feature improved support for <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/workmanager-2-5-0-stable-released-701b668cd064\">multi-process apps</a>, including performance benefits from unifying work request scheduling to a single process and limiting database growth when scheduling many requests. </p> <p> Version 2.7‚Äînow in alpha, which is targeted to the Android S SDK‚Äîprovides additional support for the platform‚Äôs new foreground restrictions. See the <a href=\"https://youtu.be/IqnCqHyu1E4\">Effective Background Tasks on Android</a> talk for more details. </p> <p> The Background Tasks Inspector is available in Android Studio Arctic Fox, allowing you to easily view and debug WorkManager jobs when using the latest versions of the library: </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/t5nL9K4vNFg/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-JSq_qgo8y3g/YKLsaUsxWKI/AAAAAAAAQhE/KcnHKap3Mb0RGlILP1HthV_wNUuFyG87gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0.png \" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"background tasts inspector\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/ https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-JSq_qgo8y3g/YKLsaUsxWKI/AAAAAAAAQhE/KcnHKap3Mb0RGlILP1HthV_wNUuFyG87gCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/pasted%2Bimage%2B0.png \" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\"> Background Tasks Inspector </p> \n    </center> <strong>Navigation</strong> <p> The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/navigation\">Navigation</a> library, Jetpack‚Äôs framework for moving between destinations in an app, now provides support for multiple backstacks and simplifies cases where destinations sit at the same depth, such as a bottom navigation bar. </p> <strong>Macrobenchmark</strong> <p> The Macrobenchmark library extends Jetpack‚Äôs benchmarking coverage to app startup and integrated behaviors like scrolling performance. The library can be used remotely to track metrics in continuous integration testing or locally with profiling results viewable from Android Studio. Check out the Google I/O talk on all the details: </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/0adLO2VRJtc\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <p> For developers who‚Äôd like to integrate more closely with Google Assistant, the Google Shortcuts library provides a way to expose actions to Google Assistant and other Google Services through the existing <code>ShortcutInfo</code> class. </p> <p> You can send up to fifteen shortcuts at a time through the <code>ShortcutManager</code> to be shown on Google Assistant, among other services, making them available for voice and other interactions. </p> <p> To implement this, define a shortcut with an <code>Intent</code> and a capability binding; this binding provides semantically-meaningful information that will help Google services figure out the best way to surface it to users. </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// expose a \"Cappuccino\" action to Google Assistant and other services\nShortcutInfoCompat siCompat =\n  ShortcutInfoCompat.Builder(ctx, \"id_cappuccino\")\n    .setShortLabel(\"Cappuccino\")\n    .setIntent(Intent(ctx, OrderCappuccino::class.java))\n    .addCapabilityBinding(\n        \"actions.intent.ORDER_MENU_ITEM\",\n        \"menuItem.name\",\n        asList(\"cappuccino\")\n    )\n    .build()\n\nShortcutManagerCompat.pushDynamicShortcut(ctx, siCompat)</pre> <strong>EmojiCompat</strong> <p> All user-generated content in your app contains üéâ, and supporting modern emoji is a key part of making your app ‚ú®! The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/look-and-feel/emoji-compat\">EmojiCompat</a> library, which supports modern emoji on API 19 and higher, has moved to a new artifact <code>:emoji2:emoji2</code>, which replaces the previous <code>:emoji:emoji</code> artifact. The new <code>emoji2</code> library adds ü™Ñ automatic configuration using the AppStartup library (you don't have to add any code üë©üèø‚Äçüíª to display üêª‚Äç‚ùÑÔ∏è)! </p> <p> AppCompat adds emoji2 starting with AppCompat 1.4. If your app uses AppCompat, users will see modern emoji ‚≠ê without any further configuration. Apps that aren't using AppCompat can add <code>:emoji2:emoji2-views</code>. For custom <code>TextViews</code>, you can support modern emoji by using the helpers in <code>:emoji2:emoji2-views-helpers</code> or by subclassing AppCompat views. </p> <h2>Jetpack Compose</h2> <p> <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/blogspot/hsDu/~3/t5nL9K4vNFg/d.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a> is Android‚Äôs modern toolkit for building native UI. It simplifies and accelerates UI development on Android. Jetpack Compose is currently in beta, and planned to go <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/05/android-12-beta-1.html\">stable in July</a>. Many of the libraries listed here, as well as others that you might already be using, have introduced features specifically for integration with Jetpack Compose. Ranging from Activity to ViewModel, Navigation, or Hilt, all of these libraries can make adopting Compose in your app smoother. Find out more about about how to use them from this Google I/O talk: </p> \n    <center> \n     <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/0z_dwBGQQWQ\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n    </center> <h2>Form factors</h2> <p> Jetpack makes it easier to work with different form factors, including foldables, large screen devices, and Wear devices. We've introduced new guidelines for large screen development along with improvements to Jetpack libraries such as <code>WindowManager</code> and <code>SlidingPaneLayout</code>. Read all the details in this <a href=\"http://goo.gle/foldables-tablets-large-screens\">blog post</a>. </p> <h2>Conclusion</h2> <p> This was a (relatively) quick overview of what‚Äôs new in Jetpack. Check out the AndroidX <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/versions\">release notes</a> for all the update details of each library and the <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc_Q7bBAqjfP9o8WvrjgvgU8\">Google I/O talks</a> for more information on some of them. </p> \n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1a2qfAD7dNM/YKGC1uH8FSI/AAAAAAAAAAw/2AKO9Tk5ArI8QEU-2WqSaNHfCG_AuqjngCPcBGAYYCw/s0/Arctic_Fox_Splash_2x.png\"><img alt=\"Android Studio Arctic Fox splash screen\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"800\" data-original-width=\"1280\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1a2qfAD7dNM/YKGC1uH8FSI/AAAAAAAAAAw/2AKO9Tk5ArI8QEU-2WqSaNHfCG_AuqjngCPcBGAYYCw/s0/Arctic_Fox_Splash_2x.png\" style=\"width:100%;\" /></a> \n <p id=\"imgCaption\">Android Studio Arctic Fox splash screen</p> \n</center> \n<p> <em>Note: As <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2020/12/announcing-android-studio-arctic-fox.html\">we announced</a> late last year, we've changed our version numbering scheme to match the number for the IntelliJ IDE that Android Studio is based on, 2020.3, plus our own patch number, as well as a handy code name to make it easier to remember and refer to. We'll be using code names in alphabetical order; the first is Arctic Fox, now in beta, and the next is Bumblebee, now in canary.</em></p> \n<p> Today, we are excited to unveil Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta ‚ùÑÔ∏èü¶ä: the latest release of the official Android IDE focuses on Design, Devices, and Developer Productivity. It is available for <a href=\"http://developer.android.com/studio/preview\">download</a> now on the beta channel for you to try out all the new features launched this week during Google I/O 2021! </p> \n<p>Inspired by developer communities around the world, who despite having to adjust to challenges this past year still continue to create amazing and innovative apps, we have delivered and updated the suite of tools to empower three major themes:</p> \n<ul> \n <li> <strong>Rapid UI design</strong> - with <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a>, it's never been easier to create modern UIs, and we have tools to help complete that journey: you can create previews in different configurations and navigate your code with Compose Preview, test it in isolation with Deploy Preview to Device, and inspect the full app with Layout inspector. Throughout iterations, you can quickly edit strings and numbers and see immediate updates. Moreover, with the Accessibility Scanner in Layout Editor, your View based layouts are audited for accessibility problems. </li> \n <li> <strong>New devices, both large and small</strong> - reimagine and extend your app beyond phones--whether it's for Wear OS, Google TV, or Android Auto, we have prepared new emulators and system images, and even authentic simulations for different testing scenarios: pair your watch and phone emulators with Wear OS Pairing, take a virtual run with Wear OS heart rate sensors, switch channels with GoogleTV Remote Control, and drive with Automotive OS Sensor Replay. </li> \n <li> <strong>Developer productivity boost</strong> - we want to ensure your workspace and environment are ready for the latest systems and optimized for speed and quality. Now you can enjoy a whole slew of new features and improvements that come with a major update to Intellij 2020.3, test your app with what Android 12 has to offer, improve your app performance with the updated UI for Memory Profiler, understand background task relationships with WorkManager Inspector, and use Non-Transitive R classes IDE Refactoring to increase build speed. </li> \n</ul> \n<p> In short, this is an upgrade you do not want to miss! ‚ú® There are many more features and improvements surrounding these themes you can find in this Beta version, so read or watch below for further highlights. Or, skip the reading, download Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta in the <a href=\"http://developer.android.com/studio/preview\">beta channel</a> and try out the latest features yourselves today! Give us feedback and help us to continue to focus on the areas you care about most in the next version of Android Studio. </p> \n<p> </p>\n<center> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/WRNWzhrl6-s\" title=\"YouTube video player\" width=\"560\"></iframe> \n <p id=\"imgCaption\">What's new in Android development tools (I/O 2021)</p> \n</center> \n<p></p> \n<br> <h1>What‚Äôs in Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta</h1> <p> Below is a full list of new features in Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta, organized by the three major themes: </p> <h2>Design</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Compose Preview</strong> - You can create previews of your Compose UI with Compose Preview! By using the @Preview annotation, Compose previews can be made to visualize multiple components at once in different configurations (i.e themes, device) as well as create a mental mapping for you to navigate your code.</li>\n </ul> \n <center>\n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HgsTXpXs61Y/YKHKhzQylkI/AAAAAAAAAA0/sNoH9D1VQ_YJ740Ng0F6lrbKmmVw500UQCLcBGAsYHQ/s2174/compose-preview-0.gif\"><img alt=\"Compose Preview\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1036\" data-original-width=\"2174\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HgsTXpXs61Y/YKHKhzQylkI/AAAAAAAAAA0/sNoH9D1VQ_YJ740Ng0F6lrbKmmVw500UQCLcBGAsYHQ/s16000/compose-preview-0.gif\" style=\"width:100%;\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Compose Preview</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Layout Inspector for Compose </strong>- You can now inspect layouts written in Compose with Layout Inspector. Whether your app uses layouts fully written in Compose or layouts that use a hybrid of Compose and Views, the Layout Inspector helps you understand how your layouts are rendered on your running device or emulator, obtain rich details (such as parameters and modifiers passed to each composable), and debug issues that might arise. As you interact with the app, you now also have the option to either enable <strong>Live Updates</strong> to constantly stream data from your device, or reduce performance impact on your device by disabling live updates and clicking the <strong>Refresh</strong> action as needed. </li>\n </ul> \n <center>\n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ik2-s2dWtX0/YKHbcYazGRI/AAAAAAAAAA8/o3-3mficEnskhDNZ0-Zxr2cUElaAajYzACLcBGAsYHQ/s2188/compose-layout-inspector.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Compose Layout Inspector\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"983\" data-original-width=\"2188\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ik2-s2dWtX0/YKHbcYazGRI/AAAAAAAAAA8/o3-3mficEnskhDNZ0-Zxr2cUElaAajYzACLcBGAsYHQ/s16000/compose-layout-inspector.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>Compose Layout Inspector</em> </p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Deploy Preview to Device </strong>- Use this feature to deploy a snippet of your UI to a device or emulator. This will help to test small parts of your code in the device without having to start the full application. Your preview will benefit the same context (permissions, resources) as your application. You can click the Deploy to device icon on the top of any Compose preview or next to the @Preview annotation in the code editor gutter and Android Studio will deploy that @Preview to your connected device or emulator. </li> \n </ul> \n <center>\n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HasZFqzsNjk/YKHf6osAzhI/AAAAAAAAABE/K3bcgcJ3j9M0_6fJOEWKDBLroBGDyMMAgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/deploy-to-device.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Using Deploy to device from preview and gutter icon\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1038\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-HasZFqzsNjk/YKHf6osAzhI/AAAAAAAAABE/K3bcgcJ3j9M0_6fJOEWKDBLroBGDyMMAgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/deploy-to-device.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>Using Deploy to device from preview and gutter icon</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Live Edit of literals </strong>- Live Editing of literals allows developers using Compose to quickly edit literals (strings, numbers, booleans) in their code and see the results immediately without needing to wait for compilation. The goal of the feature is to increase your productivity by having code changes appear near instantaneously in the previews, emulator, or physical device. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-7SU-OGLKV9E/YKHhg8JBCjI/AAAAAAAAABM/ziGPUmgqQMQMhIhAE-LfhcDhar24jf5HACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/live-editing-of-literals.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Editing numbers and strings update immediately in the preview and on device\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1088\" data-original-width=\"2188\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-7SU-OGLKV9E/YKHhg8JBCjI/AAAAAAAAABM/ziGPUmgqQMQMhIhAE-LfhcDhar24jf5HACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/live-editing-of-literals.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>Editing numbers and strings update immediately in the preview and on device</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Accessibility Scanner for Layout Editor </strong>- Android Studio now integrates with the Android Accessibility Test Framework to help you find accessibility issues in your layouts. When using the Layout Editor, click on the error report button to launch the panel. The tool will report accessibility related issues and also offers suggested fixes for some common problems (e.g. missing content descriptions, or low contrast) </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qGv1PC57qRg/YKHjFrZGDqI/AAAAAAAAABU/vQnfQwW7MCkVVYiAxhWtkzEOZ-ejiVKkgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/atf-scanner.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Accessibility Test Framework Scanner in Layout Editor\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1085\" data-original-width=\"1924\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qGv1PC57qRg/YKHjFrZGDqI/AAAAAAAAABU/vQnfQwW7MCkVVYiAxhWtkzEOZ-ejiVKkgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/atf-scanner.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"> <em>Accessibility Test Framework Scanner in Layout Editor</em></p> \n </center> <h2>Devices</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Wear OS Pairing </strong>- We created a new Wear OS pairing assistant to guide developers step by step through pairing Wear OS emulators with physical or virtual phones directly in Android Studio! You can start by going to <strong><em>device dropdown &gt; Wear OS emulator pairing assistant</em></strong>. Note that this will currently pair with Wear OS 2 companion, and Wear OS 3 will be coming soon. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/apps/creating#pairing-assistant\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Learn more</a>. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-6raF4npOXDE/YKHlQNU0vuI/AAAAAAAAABc/-cUsjnNsBPYxDpzkdqPZ_B_gkJFzxmNwgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/wearOS-pairing-dialog.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:450px\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Wear OS emulator pairing assistant dialog\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1536\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-6raF4npOXDE/YKHlQNU0vuI/AAAAAAAAABc/-cUsjnNsBPYxDpzkdqPZ_B_gkJFzxmNwgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/wearOS-pairing-dialog.png\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Wear OS emulator pairing assistant dialog</em></p> \n  <!--this image width is 100% - the GDoc original displays it smaller--> \n </center> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-vtTQcPuerek/YKHm8ITnssI/AAAAAAAAABk/Ttb9hbWlZCEwsOYIluQlzkTgtAjyYVZ4QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/WearOS-pairing-1.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Phone + Watch emulators paired successful state\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1159\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-vtTQcPuerek/YKHm8ITnssI/AAAAAAAAABk/Ttb9hbWlZCEwsOYIluQlzkTgtAjyYVZ4QCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/WearOS-pairing-1.png\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Phone + Watch emulators paired successful state</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>New Wear OS system images</strong> - a developer preview of the Wear OS 3 system image is now available so that you can use and play with the newest version of Wear OS! </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X5mdOT7zw3c/YKHoO62rX_I/AAAAAAAAABs/6An3tQcZ5HE9u4-VznoFG0atNdxy6c8qACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/WearOS-new-emulator.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:350px\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Wear OS system image\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1150\" data-original-width=\"994\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-X5mdOT7zw3c/YKHoO62rX_I/AAAAAAAAABs/6An3tQcZ5HE9u4-VznoFG0atNdxy6c8qACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/WearOS-new-emulator.png\" /></a> \n  <!--This image is 400px instead of 100%--> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Wear OS system image</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Heart Rate Sensor for Wear OS Emulators</strong> - To help you test your Wear OS apps, the Android Emulator now has support for the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/hardware/Sensor#TYPE_HEART_RATE\">Heart Rate Sensor API</a> when you run the Wear OS emulator. <em>Make sure you are running at least Android Emulator v30.4.5 downloaded via the Android Studio SDK Manager</em> </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-btv93xVse-0/YKQlHdHb9DI/AAAAAAAAQkE/ievzGogMVJEn4OhTpb8QBP7Fac80lE5gQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/heart_rate%2B%25281%2529.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Heart Rate Sensor for Wear OS Emulators\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"240\" data-original-width=\"512\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-btv93xVse-0/YKQlHdHb9DI/AAAAAAAAQkE/ievzGogMVJEn4OhTpb8QBP7Fac80lE5gQCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/heart_rate%2B%25281%2529.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Heart Rate Sensor for Wear OS Emulators</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Google TV Remote Control</strong> - On top of running the new Google TV UI, we now have an updated Remote control panel, which has mapping for the new Google TV remote controls features like: user profile, and settings. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IwIR8Dx_j30/YKHuiM4LoTI/AAAAAAAAAB0/24YAAIzRp7MxgfYAmUAX2sT7UI3Cp8ZbgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-tv-remote-short.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Google TV remote controls\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"899\" data-original-width=\"2240\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IwIR8Dx_j30/YKHuiM4LoTI/AAAAAAAAAB0/24YAAIzRp7MxgfYAmUAX2sT7UI3Cp8ZbgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/google-tv-remote-short.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Google TV remote controls</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>New Google TV system images</strong> - We have updated the system images to reflect the new Google TV experience allowing you to freely explore the UI. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oVCPha8vw-8/YKHxx6GrJxI/AAAAAAAAAB8/CBY-yKw7kiMXS5aXqyswYk76BXdUDLIiwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Google%2BTV%2Bemulator%2Bwith%2BTenet.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Google TV system image\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"809\" data-original-width=\"1392\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oVCPha8vw-8/YKHxx6GrJxI/AAAAAAAAAB8/CBY-yKw7kiMXS5aXqyswYk76BXdUDLIiwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/Google%2BTV%2Bemulator%2Bwith%2BTenet.png\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Google TV system image</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Automotive OS Sensor Replay</strong> - You can now use the Android Automotive emulator to simulate driving scenarios, with the ability to replay car sensor data (e.g. speed, gear), completing your development and testing workflow. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Oy_Um-o9J5k/YKHycKCkCDI/AAAAAAAAACE/eviq0Y0v7fY0JnF7gt28qJrVV6yGOjeMwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-auto-sensor.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Android Automotive OS Sensor replay\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1039\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Oy_Um-o9J5k/YKHycKCkCDI/AAAAAAAAACE/eviq0Y0v7fY0JnF7gt28qJrVV6yGOjeMwCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/android-auto-sensor.png\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Android Automotive OS Sensor replay</em></p> \n </center> <h2>Developer Productivity</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>IntelliJ Platform Update </strong>- Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta includes the IntelliJ 2020.3 platform release üòé, which has many new features such as Debugger interactive hints, new Welcome screen, and a ton of new code editor enhancements to speed up your workflow. <a href=\"https://blog.jetbrains.com/idea/2020/12/intellij-idea-2020-3/\">Learn more</a>. </li> \n </ul> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Android 12 lint checks</strong> - We‚Äôve added lint checks that are specific to building your app for Android 12 so that you can get guidance in context. To name a few -- we have built checks for custom declarations of splash screens, coarse location permission for fine location usage, media formats, and high sensor sampling rate permission. </li> \n </ul> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Non-transitive R classes Refactoring</strong> - Using non-transitive R classes with the Android Gradle Plugin can lead to faster builds for applications with multiple modules. It prevents resource duplication by ensuring that each module only contains references to its own resources, without pulling references from dependencies. You can access this feature by going to <strong><em>Refactor &gt; Migrate to Non-transitive R Classes.</em></strong> </li> \n </ul> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Apple Silicon Support Preview</strong> - For those using MacOS on Apple Silicon (arm64) hardware, Android Studio Arctic Fox provides preview support for this new architecture.&nbsp; The arm64 platform support is still under active development, but we wanted to provide you a release order to get your feedback. Since this is a preview release for the arm64 architecture, you will have to separately download this version from the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/archive\">Android Studio download archive</a> page and look for <em>Mac (Apple Silicon)</em>. </li> \n </ul> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Extended controls in the Emulator tool window</strong> - Developers now have access to all extended emulator controls when the emulator is opened in a tool window. The extended controls will give developers powerful tools for testing their apps such as navigation playback, virtual sensors, and snapshots all within Android studio. To launch the Emulator within Android Studio go to Android Studio's <strong><em>Preferences &gt; Tools &gt; Emulator </em></strong>and select ‚ÄúLaunch in a tool window.\" </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tsWqiUC0K4o/YKH0-JKl7TI/AAAAAAAAACM/tXrlPTUosxM6dQjxr_cFHd3Wxqp_SDfvgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/emulator-extended-control.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Extended controls in the Emulator tool window\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1152\" data-original-width=\"2048\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tsWqiUC0K4o/YKH0-JKl7TI/AAAAAAAAACM/tXrlPTUosxM6dQjxr_cFHd3Wxqp_SDfvgCLcBGAsYHQ/s0/emulator-extended-control.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Extended controls in the Emulator tool window</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Background Task Inspector</strong> - You can now utilize the Background Task Inspector to visualize, monitor, and debug your app's background workers when using <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/work\">WorkManager library</a> 2.5.0 or higher. You can access it by going to<strong><em> View &gt; Tool Windows &gt; App Inspection</em></strong> from the menu bar. When you deploy an app on a device running API level 26 and higher, you should see active workers in the Background Task Inspector tab, as shown below. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/r/studio-ui/background-task-inspector-help\">Learn more</a>. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TFdmnYj7fZA/YKH2XMWtlsI/AAAAAAAAACU/2c-9kXDkkzU1-p_NIWTCGgSwJS5ETX0aACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/work-manager.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Background Task Inspector\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"672\" data-original-width=\"2189\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TFdmnYj7fZA/YKH2XMWtlsI/AAAAAAAAACU/2c-9kXDkkzU1-p_NIWTCGgSwJS5ETX0aACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/work-manager.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Background Task Inspector</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Parallel device testing with Test Matrix</strong> - Instrumentation tests can now be run across multiple devices in parallel and investigated using a new specialized instrumentation test results panel, called the Test Matrix, which streams the test results in real time. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/preview/features#instrumentation-testing\">Learn more</a> </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Pw1uOUO1ri4/YKH3l161H4I/AAAAAAAAACc/ThLsMB4RwWoElGmproKZ42v6OxswRB7UACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/test-matrix.png\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Test matrix running tests across multiple devices in parallel\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"860\" data-original-width=\"3282\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Pw1uOUO1ri4/YKH3l161H4I/AAAAAAAAACc/ThLsMB4RwWoElGmproKZ42v6OxswRB7UACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/test-matrix.png\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Test matrix running tests across multiple devices in parallel</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Memory Profiler new recording UI</strong> - We have consolidated the Memory Profiler UI for different recording activities, such as capturing a heap dump and recording Java, Kotlin, and native memory allocations. </li> \n </ul> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jl5ifLYdzUE/YKH4cnJOQwI/AAAAAAAAACk/pAePwaXwwSI3P1qc1O3OlYwPtr2KLyM5ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/memory-profiler-record.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" id=\"imgFull\" alt=\"Memory Profiler: recorded Java / Kotlin Allocations\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"949\" data-original-width=\"1529\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jl5ifLYdzUE/YKH4cnJOQwI/AAAAAAAAACk/pAePwaXwwSI3P1qc1O3OlYwPtr2KLyM5ACLcBGAsYHQ/s0/memory-profiler-record.gif\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\"><em>Memory Profiler: recorded Java / Kotlin Allocations</em></p> \n </center> \n <ul> \n  <li> <strong>Updated system requirements</strong> - In order to ensure that we provide the best experience for Android developers, we are updating the system requirements when using Android Studio. These requirements also represent the configurations we use to thoroughly test Android Studio to maintain high quality and performance, and we plan to update them more frequently going forward. So, while you‚Äôre still able to use systems that fall below the requirements, we can‚Äôt guarantee compatibility or support when doing so. You can see the <a href=\"https://developers.android.com/studio#Requirements\">updated system requirements</a> on the official developer site. </li> \n </ul> <p> To recap, Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) Beta includes these new enhancements &amp; features: </p> <h2>Design</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li>Compose Preview</li> \n  <li>Compose Layout Inspector</li> \n  <li>Deploy Preview to Device</li> \n  <li>Live Edit of literals</li> \n  <li>Accessibility Scanner in Layout Editor</li> \n </ul> <h2>Devices</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li>Wear OS Pairing</li> \n  <li>Heart Rate Sensor</li> \n  <li>New Wear OS system images</li> \n  <li>Google TV Remote Control</li> \n  <li>Google TV system Images</li> \n  <li>Automotive OS Sensor Replay</li> \n </ul> <h2>Productivity</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li>Intellij 2020.3.1</li> \n  <li>Android 12 lint checks</li> \n  <li>Non-transitive R classes Refactoring</li> \n  <li>Apple Silicon Support Preview</li> \n  <li>Android Emulator Extended Controls</li> \n  <li>Background Task Inspector</li> \n  <li>Test matrix</li> \n  <li>Memory Profiler new recording UI</li> \n </ul> <p> You might also have seen other new features at I/O which are not included in the list above; they are included in Android Studio (2021.1.1) Bumblebee Canary since these features were not quite ready for a beta channel release: </p> <h2>Design</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li>Interactive Compose preview</li> \n  <li>Compose Animation preview</li> \n  <li>Preview Configuration Picker</li> \n  <li>Animated vector drawable preview</li> \n  <li>Compose Blueprint Mode</li> \n  <li>Compose Constraints Preview for ConstraintLayout</li> \n </ul> <h2>Devices</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li> Automotive OS USB Passthrough - <em>Coming soon</em> </li> \n  <li> Automotive OS Rotary Controls - <em>Coming soon</em> </li> \n </ul> <h2>Productivity</h2> \n <ul> \n  <li>Kotlin Coroutines debugger</li> \n  <li>Device Manager</li> \n  <li>Gradle Instrumented Test Runner Integration in Android Studio</li> \n  <li>Gradle Managed Devices</li> \n </ul> <br> <h1>Sessions at Google I/O 2021</h1> <p> With this exciting release, the Android Studio team also presented a series of sessions about Android Studio. Watch the following videos to see the latest features in action and to get tips &amp; tricks on how to use Android Studio üì∫: </p> \n  <ul> \n   <li> <a href=\"https://youtu.be/WRNWzhrl6-s\">What's new in Android development tools</a> </li> \n   <li> <a href=\"https://youtu.be/etLUpHvhNZw\">State of Kotlin on Android</a> </li> \n   <li> <a href=\"https://youtu.be/B1u7JZ1rLyE\">What‚Äôs new in design tools</a> </li> \n   <li> <a href=\"https://youtu.be/AZBW5StgF8o\">What‚Äôs new in Android gradle plugin</a> </li> \n   <li> <a href=\"https://youtu.be/juEkViDyzF8\">What's new in Android testing tools</a> </li> \n  </ul> <br> <h1>Getting Started</h1> <p> Android Studio Arctic Fox (2020.3.1) is a big release, and now is a good time to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/preview\">download</a> and check out the Beta release to incorporate the new features into your workflow. The beta release is near stable release quality, but as with any beta release, bugs may still exist, so, if you do find an issue, let us know so we can work to fix it. If you‚Äôre already using Android Studio, you can check for updates on the Beta channel from the navigation menu <strong><em>(Help &gt; Check for Update [Windows/Linux] , Android Studio &gt; Check for Updates [OS X])</em></strong>. When you update to beta, you will get access to the new version of Android Studio and Android Emulator. </p> <p> As always, we appreciate any feedback on things you like, and issues or features you would like to see. If you find a bug or issue, please file an issue. Follow us -- the Android Studio development team -- on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/androidstudio\">Twitter</a> and on <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers\" rel=\"noopener\">Medium</a>.
